Appeal denied by, Petition denied by Commonwealth v. Bell, 557 Pa. 624, 732 A.2d 611, 1998 Pa. LEXIS 2468 (1998)
Post-conviction proceeding at Commonwealth v. Bell, L., 2012 Pa. Super. LEXIS 3868 (Pa. Super. Ct., Aug. 10, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Post Conviction Relief Act November 26, 1996 in the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, Criminal No. 8204-0297-1/1, 0304. Before PAPALINI, J.
COMMONWEALTH v. BELL, 343 Pa. Super. 604, 494 A.2d 476, 1985 Pa. Super. LEXIS 8965 (1985)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the order of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), which denied his petition for relief under the Post-Conviction Relief Act (PCRA), 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 9541 et seq. Appellant alleged that the PCRA court erred when it found that the commonwealth would have been prejudiced if it retried appellant.


OVERVIEW: Appellant and co-defendant conspired to rob a drug dealer. The dealer was stabbed, but escaped; co-defendant fatally stabbed a victim. Appellant was convicted of second-degree murder, robbery, aggravated assault, and conspiracy. His petition under the Post-Conviction Relief Act (PCRA), 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 9541 et seq., was denied. On appeal, the court determined that appellant's claim of after-discovered evidence that co-defendant killed the victim for personal reasons unrelated to the robbery was cognizable under the PCRA. However, because appellant waited six years to file his petition, the case was remanded to determine whether commonwealth would be prejudiced if it retried appellant. On remand, the PCRA court determined that commonwealth would be prejudiced because of the unavailability of the drug dealer and other witnesses. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that commonwealth, without its key eyewitness, would be hampered in its ability to rebut appellant's theory, which was untested at the original trial. The court concluded that the PCRA was not designed to afford appellant an opportunity to present a new defense unanswerable due to the passage of time.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of appellant's petition for relief under the Post-Conviction Relief Act because commonwealth would have been prejudiced in its ability to retry appellant because the only eyewitness to the events that led to the murder was no longer available.

Commonwealth v. Gindlesperger


No. 00085 Pittsburgh 1997


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


706 A.2d 1216; 1997 Pa. Super. LEXIS 3860


June 24, 1997, Argued  
December 24, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Allowance of Appeal Granted June 15, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Pa. LEXIS 1192.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence of February 14, 1996. In the Court of Common Pleas of Erie County Criminal Division, No. 01515-1994. Before CONNELLY, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of sentence vacated; denial of motion to suppress is reversed; jurisdiction relinquished.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his conviction by the Court of Common Pleas of Erie County (Pennsylvania), for possession of marijuana. Appellant asserted that the search warrant used to gather incriminating against him was unsupported by sufficient and permissible probable cause because it was based upon information provided by an informant and an infrared thermal detection device.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of possession of marijuana and manufacture of a controlled substance, and took an appeal nunc pro tunc. The main issue was whether the search warrant was legal where probable cause was based upon information provided by an informant and the results from an infrared thermal detection device aimed at appellant's house. The court vacated the judgment of sentence and reversed the denial of appellant's pretrial motion to suppress. The court found that the lower court erred in failing to suppress the results of the search. The court concluded that the use of the infrared thermal detection device violated the U.S. Const. amend. IV, and accordingly, that portion of the search warrant affidavit which relied upon its use was invalid. The court also concluded that the information in the affidavit, which was provided by a confidential informant, did not establish probable cause for issuance of the search warrant because it was not properly supported by other evidence or proof of the reliability of the informant, and thus, the search warrant was not supported by probable cause.


OUTCOME: The court vacated appellant's conviction and reversed the denial of appellant's motion to suppress because the search warrant was not based upon legally sufficient probable cause, where the informant's reliability was not established, and an infrared thermal detection device had been illegally used to invade appellant's home.

Cons. Stat. § 9715. Appellant contended that he acted in self-defense and that the statute was not intended to apply when the crime triggering the statute occurred subsequent to the crime for which the life sentence was imposed.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was found guilty of third degree murder for a Pennsylvania murder. While he was a fugitive and not yet arrested, he committed two homicides in New York. Commonwealth v. Fisher


No. 919 Philadelphia 1997


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


703 A.2d 714; 1997 Pa. Super. LEXIS 3833


November 14, 1997, Submitted  
December 9, 1997, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the ORDER ENTERED February 06, 1997 In the Court of Common Pleas of MONROE County, CRIMINAL, No. NO. 385 CR 1992. Before O'BRIEN, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the order of the Court of Common Pleas of Monroe County (Pennsylvania), that denied his petition for post-conviction relief under the Post Conviction Relief Act. 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 9541 et seq after his conviction for wiretapping.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of nine counts of wiretapping and was sentenced to county imprisonment and a fine. The sentence was affirmed on direct appeal. Appellant was sent after 20 months to a state institution to serve a concurrent sentence of 11 to 23 years for fraudulent real estate transactions. Stat. § 9541 et seq., and the commonwealth filed a motion to dismiss on the ground that appellant had completed serving his sentence. The trial court ordered the petition dismissed. The court affirmed the order of the trial court because it found that the PCRA only afforded relief to those who were currently serving a sentence of imprisonment, probation, or parole for the crime pursuant to 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 9543(a)(1). Even though appellant had the potential to be punished for contempt if he was able to pay his fines, but did not, he was not eligible for post-conviction relief pursuant to the PCRA.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court because it found that the Post Conviction Relief Act only afforded relief to those who were currently serving a sentence of imprisonment, probation, or parole for the crime. Even though appellant had the potential to be punished for contempt if he was able to pay his fines, but did not, he was not eligible for post-conviction relief pursuant to the act when the only remaining sentence was a fine.

Commonwealth v. Graham


No. 2889 Philadelphia 1996


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


703 A.2d 510; 1997 Pa. Super. LEXIS 3704



November 25, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Allowance of Appeal Denied May 13, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Pa. LEXIS 963.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence Dated July 18, 1996, In the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, Criminal, No. 1357 AUG. TERM 1994. Before RICHETTE, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgement of sentence affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Court of Common Pleas, Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), convicting him of homicide by vehicle while driving under the influence of alcohol or a controlled substance and driving under the influence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed a conviction of homicide by vehicle while driving under the influence of alcohol or a controlled substance and driving under the influence in violation of 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 3731. Defendant contended that his trial counsel was ineffective for failing to make a motion to suppress the results of a blood test on the grounds that 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 1547(e), which made a refusal to submit to a blood test admissible at trial, violated his right not to incriminate himself under U.S. Const. amend. V. Defendant alleged that the underlying consent to the test was coerced because it was given out of fear that a refusal would be introduced at trial. The court on appeal affirmed, holding that defendant failed to establish a claim of ineffective assistance of counsel because he could not demonstrate that his motion to suppress had arguable merit. Defendant had no constitutional right to refuse the blood test and thus § 1547(e) did not burden his constitutional rights by allowing evidence of his refusal to consent to be admitted at trial. The consent was therefore valid.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the convictions of homicide by vehicle while driving under the influence of alcohol or a controlled substance and driving under the influence, holding that defendant failed to establish a claim for ineffective assistance of counsel because the underlying claim that the statute permitting evidence of a refusal to consent to a blood test to be admitted at trial was without merit.

Pellish v. Gerhart


No. 02068 Pittsburgh 1996


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


701 A.2d 594; 1997 Pa. Super. LEXIS 3378



October 30, 1997, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Clearfield County, Family Division at No. 91-319-S.D. Before AMMERMAN, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father sought review of a decision of the Court of Common Pleas, Family Division, Clearfield County (Pennsylvania), which granted appellee mother's petition for modification of a child support order. Appellant asserted that the lower court erred in requiring him to contribute to the child's tuition.


OVERVIEW: Appellant father challenged a trial court decision, which granted appellee mother's petition for modification of a child support order. Appellant asserted that the lower court erred in requiring him to contribute to the child's private school tuition. As part of a divorce settlement, appellee mother received $ 300.00 per week in child support, and had primary physical and legal custody of the parties minor children. After the divorce, appellee moved for modification as the child was removed from public school and placed in private school. Appellant father contended that precedent prohibited the lower court from requiring him to contribute and that appellee failed to establish it was a reasonable expense under Pa. Con. Stat. Ann. § 1910.16-5(1). The court affirmed and held that the trial court did not err in concluding that private schooling for the child was consistent with the family's standard of living. The court held that appellant father had to contribute to the child private school tuition.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in favor of appellee mother, holding that the trial court did not err in concluding that private schooling for the child was consistent with the family's standard of living. The court held that appellant father had to contribute to the child private school tuition.

Commonwealth v. Greene


No. 02093 Pittsburgh, 1996, No. 02094 Pittsburgh, 1996


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA

June 9, 1997, Submitted  
September 30, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Reargument Denied December 12, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeals from the P.C.R.A. and Order of the Court of Common Pleas, Westmoreland County, Criminal Division, at No. 1190 C 1994. Before BLAHOVEC, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of sentence vacated. Remanded with directives. Jurisdiction relinquished. Appeal at No. 02093 Pittsburgh 1996 dismissed as moot.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the orders of the Court of Common Pleas, Westmoreland County (Pennsylvania), which convicted him of robbery pursuant to 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 3701(a)(1)(ii), criminal conspiracy pursuant to 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 903(a), and receiving stolen property pursuant to 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 3925(a).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of robbery under 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 3701(a)(1)(ii), criminal conspiracy under 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 903(a), and receiving stolen property under 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 3925(a) and sentenced to an aggregate period of 10 and one half to 21 years of imprisonment. Defendant was granted a right to direct appeal nunc pro tunc and appealed the judgment of sentence nunc pro tunc. The court vacated the judgment of sentence and remanded, holding that it was error to impose the deadly weapon enhancement under 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 9712(a) because defendant received a guidelines sentence which required that the weapon be in his possession or immediate control for the enhancement to apply. The court also found that defendant received ineffective assistance because counsel improperly commingled her attack on the sufficiency of the evidence with defendant's challenge to the weight of the evidence. However, the court held that the method of juror selection was not unconstitutional because the county used non-discriminatory driver's license and voter registration lists. Further, the evidence was sufficient to show that defendant conspired to commit robbery.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the judgment of sentence and remanded. The court held that the deadly weapon enhancement did not apply to defendant because he received a guidelines sentence which only allowed the enhancement if defendant was in possession or control of a weapon at the time of the offense. The court also found that defendant received ineffective assistance of counsel.

Commonwealth v. Curran


No. 2415 Pittsburgh 1996


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


700 A.2d 1333; 1997 Pa. Super. LEXIS 3203


July 14, 1997, Submitted  
September 29, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As corrected November 25, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from JUDGMENT OF SENTENCE November 26, 1996, Docketed December 3, 1996, in the Court of Common Pleas of ARMSTRONG County, CRIMINAL DIVISION, No. 1996-0089. Before NICKLEACH, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of sentence affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Court of Common Pleas of Armstrong County (Pennsylvania), which convicted him of driving while under the influence of alcohol pursuant to 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 3731(a)(1), and homicide by vehicle while driving under the influence pursuant to 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 3735.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his convictions for driving while under the influence of alcohol under 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 3731(a)(1), and homicide by vehicle while driving under the influence under 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 3735. Defendant argued that the Commonwealth was required to introduce expert testimony to relate back the blood alcohol content to the time he was driving. The court affirmed and held that no expert relation back testimony was needed in defendant's prosecution pursuant to § 3731(a)(1). Under § 3731(a)(1), defendant could be convicted despite the fact that his blood alcohol level could not be related back to the time of his driving. In prosecutions under § 3731(a)(1) the delay between the operation of the motor vehicle and when the blood was drawn goes only to the weight of the evidence and not its admissibility. Thus, there was no error in admitting defendant's blood alcohol content without expert relation back testimony.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for driving while under the influence of alcohol and homicide by vehicle while driving under the influence. The court held that to convict defendant for driving while under the influence, the Commonwealth was not required to present testimony to relate the defendant's blood alcohol level back to the time of his driving.

Commonwealth v. Anders


No. 652 Harrisburg 1996


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


699 A.2d 1258; 1997 Pa. Super. LEXIS 2832


April 7, 1997, Submitted  
August 22, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Allowance of Appeal Granted February 20, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Pa. LEXIS 246.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence, August 1, 1996, Docketed August 6, 1996, in the Court of Common Pleas of Huntingdon County, Criminal Division, No. 95-504 CA. Before KURTZ, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought en banc review of a judgment of the Court of Common Pleas of Huntingdon County (Pennsylvania), which sentenced appellant to imprisonment for 30 days to 23 months on his conviction for driving under the influence of alcohol in violation of 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. §3731(a)(5), despite appellant's contention that the trial court failed to timely sentence him without good cause for the delay as required by Pa. R. Crim. P. 1405.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, convicted of driving under the influence of alcohol pursuant to 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 3731(a)(5), challenged the trial court's judgment of sentence more than 37 days after the 60-day sentencing limit imposed by Pa. R. Crim. P. 1405(A) had expired. Appellant argued that he was not timely sentenced under Rule 1405(A), and that under Commonwealth v. Thomas, 449 Pa. Super. 646, 674 A.2d 1119 (1996), the proper remedy for a Rule 1405(A) violation was discharge. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, holding that although the trial court did not timely sentence appellant under Rule 1405(A) because it provided no explanation on the record for the delay, discharge was not the appropriate remedy. The court expressly overruled Thomas to the extent it held that discharge was an appropriate remedy for a Rule 1405(A) violation, because Rule 1405(A) provided no remedy for its violation, much less the ultimate remedy of discharge, and because the case conflicted with the framework developed for analyzing claims of untimely sentencing. Appellant waived any speedy trial or due process challenges because he failed to argue that his protected interests were violated.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment sentencing appellant to imprisonment on his conviction for driving under the influence of alcohol, and held that even though the trial court failed to timely sentence him following his conviction, discharge from the sentence was not an appropriate remedy, and the court expressly overruled a case so holding. The court ruled that appellant failed to preserve his speedy trial and due process challenges.

 

248 of 892 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Heggenstaller


NO. 00714 HARRISBURG, 1996


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


699 A.2d 767; 1997 Pa. Super. LEXIS 2634


June 19, 1997, Argued  
August 8, 1997, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence in the Court of Common Pleas of Centre County, Criminal Division, No. A85412. Before GRINE, J.



DISPOSITION: Conviction affirmed; judgment of sentence vacated; case remanded for reimposition of fines in accordance with this Opinion. Jurisdiction relinquished.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from the Court of Common Pleas of Centre County (Pennsylvania), which convicted appellant of failing to pay $ 1.25 per month on his telephone bill for 911 emergency services and imposed an aggregate fine in the amount of $ 6,591.25.


OVERVIEW: Appellant challenged a judgment from the trial court, which found him guilty of nonpayment of 911 fees. On appeal, the court affirmed appellant's conviction, but reversed the trial court's judgment as to the amount fined. The court found sufficient evidence was presented to sustain appellant's conviction but found that the fines imposed by the trial court were extremely excessive in light of the de minimus nature of the violation. Specifically, appellant was found guilty of not paying $ 1.25 per month from the period of March 1993 through December 1995, which amounted to $ 28.75. However, the trial court imposed an additional penalty of $ 6,550, which was the equivalent of more than 430 years of unpaid 911 charges. The court held that a fine should be sufficient enough to discourage the conduct, but not so excessive as to be punitive in nature and that here the fine was unreasonable and excessive. The court remanded to the trial court for reimposition of a fine more in line with the violation and directed the trial court to make an on-the-record determination regarding appellant's financial resources and his ability to pay the imposed fine.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for failure to pay 911 fees, but vacated the trial court's judgment and remanded for reimposition of fines, because the fine in excess of $ 6,000 was unreasonable and excessive in light of the $ 1.25 monthly fee and the fact that it amounted to 430 years of unpaid 911 charges.

Commonwealth v. Stark


No. 02284 Pittsburgh 1996


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


698 A.2d 1327; 1997 Pa. Super. LEXIS 2630


May 19, 1997, Submitted  
August 6, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Revised August 27, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the PCRA Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Westmoreland County, Criminal Division at 2797 C 1991. Before MCCORMICK, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Westmoreland County (Pennsylvania), which accepted his plea of guilty for burglary and theft by unlawful taking and denied defendant's petition for relief pursuant to the Post Conviction Relief Act, 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 9541.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of burglary and theft by unlawful taking after entering a plea of guilty. Defendant sought review of a trial court order which denied his petition for relief pursuant to the Post Conviction Relief Act, 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 9541. Defendant alleged that he was unlawfully induced to enter a plea agreement because he was not aware of the consequences of his plea. On review, the court affirmed. The court found that defendant had no constitutional right to parole and thus rejected defendant's claim that his plea was involuntary because changes in parole board rules had allegedly increased his effective minimum sentence. The court held that the trial court need not advise a defendant pleading guilty of the rules of the Pennsylvania Board of Probation and Parole and/or the possibility of parole upon expiration of a minimum period of incarceration. The court defined eligibility for parole as a collateral consequence of defendant's plea, and not a constitutional right. The court found that a constitutional issue would only arise if the parole statute provided an expectation of release, and the Pennsylvania statute did not create any such expectation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court, which denied defendant's requested relief pursuant to the Post Conviction Relief Act, because the court found that defendant's guilty plea was knowing and voluntary, despite the trial court's failure to advise defendant of the circumstances affecting parole and the changes in release rules of the parole board after defendant was sentenced.

Commonwealth v. Petroll

SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA

February 18, 1997, Submitted  
June 18, 1997, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Allowance of Appeal Denied October 10, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Pa. LEXIS 2108.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence of June 28, 1996. In the Court of Common Pleas of Lancaster County, Criminal Division, No. 2616-1995. Before STENGEL, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of sentence affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from judgment entered, in the Court of Common Pleas, Lancaster County (Pennsylvania), after a jury found him guilty of three counts of homicide by vehicle, under 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 3732, and the trial court found him guilty of one count each of failing to drive his vehicle at safe speed, violating 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 3361, and careless driving, violating 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 3714.


OVERVIEW: Defendant caused the deaths of three people by driving a tractor-trailer into their car, which was stopped in traffic. He was convicted of homicide by vehicle, failing to drive at a safe speed, and careless driving. He appealed, and the court affirmed, finding sufficient evidence to support the verdict. The court held while police could have inspected a book and two bags found in his truck after the accident, their warrantless seizure was improper, and the items should have been suppressed. Other items, such as a radar detector, were in plain view, and properly seized. Due to the totality of evidence, the court held that the denial below of the suppression motion was harmless error. The court also approved of rulings concerning the admission of the radar detector, as it went to intent to violate speed restrictions; sustained the exclusion of evidence concerning road signs, and the qualification of an expert witness, as not an abuse of the lower court's discretion; and sustained rulings relating to use of accident scene photographs at trial, because defendant failed to include the photographs in the record, and the court could not assess his claim concerning them.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the verdict convicting defendant of homicide by vehicle, failing to drive at a safe speed, and careless driving. There was sufficient evidence to support the verdict, and lower court rulings concerning admission of items seized from defendant's truck after the accident, were either correct or, if erroneous, resulted in harmless error.

Commonwealth v. Bershad


No. 0224 Harrisburg, 1996


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


693 A.2d 1303; 1997 Pa. Super. LEXIS 799


January 7, 1997, Argued  
April 3, 1997, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence entered October 13, 1995, Court of Common Pleas, Dauphin County, Criminal Division at No. 2326 CD 1994. Before LEWIS, J.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his conviction and sentence before the Court of Common Pleas, Dauphin County (Pennsylvania), for theft by failure to make required disposition of funds received under 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 3927(a).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was prosecuted for theft by failure to make required disposition of funds received under 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 3927(a) for his failure to remit taxes on a corporation's behalf. He challenged the conviction. Although defendant obtained the funds in another county, because the Department of Revenue was due taxes, subject matter jurisdiction and venue were proper in the county wherein the department was located. The court held that § 3927(a) was not void for vagueness, as the statute sufficiently set forth the elements, and the statute did not unconstitutionally shift burdens, as it required the state to prove the elements beyond a reasonable doubt. The court held defendant could be charged under the general provision of § 3927 instead of the specific provision of the Tax Reform Code, 72 P.S. § 7268(b), as the contrast between the two was obvious and thus the rule to not permit prosecutions under general provisions when there are special provisions available did not apply. The court held that defendant failed to demonstrate a substantial question with regard to his sentence, and thus declined to address the claims. The court affirmed defendant's conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence for theft by failure to make required disposition of funds received. Because the Department of Revenue was due taxes, subject matter jurisdiction and venue were proper wherein the department was located. Defendant was properly charged under a general provision of the code rather than a special provision, as the general prohibition against such did not apply as the statutes were different.

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Allowance of Appeal Denied October 16, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Pa. LEXIS 2129.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County, Criminal Division at No. CC 9505084. Before LITTLE, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of sentence affirmed in part; reversed in part; jurisdiction relinquished.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County (Pennsylvania), convicting him of driving while under the influence of alcohol. Defendant claimed that the results of his breathalyzer test should have been suppressed and that his conviction was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the results of his breathalyzer test should have been suppressed, as the machine used to test his alcohol level had registered a variance while testing previous subjects, and that the subsequent calibration and testing of the machine, without any adjustments or repairs, was insufficient to show that his breath test was done in accordance with the procedures prescribed in 67 Pa. Code §§ 77.21-77.27. Defendant also asserted that his conviction for driving while under the influence, pursuant to 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 3731(a)(5), was unconstitutional. The court affirmed the denial of defendant's motion to suppress, holding that because the breathalyzer machine passed the accuracy and calibration tests, it was not necessary for the machine to be serviced, repaired, or adjusted. The court vacated the portion of defendant's conviction under 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 3731(a)(5), because that statute had previously been declared unconstitutional by the supreme court. However, because the trial court had only imposed a penalty for defendant's conviction under 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 3731(a)(4), the court held that it was unnecessary the case to be remanded for resentencing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of defendant's motion to suppress his breathalyzer test results, holding that because the breathalyzer machine had passed accuracy and calibration tests, the test on defendant complied with the requirements of both the statute and regulations. However, the court vacated one portion of defendant's conviction, because part of the drunk driving statute had previously been held unconstitutional by the supreme court.

State of the Art Med. Prods. v. Aries Med.


NO. 244 PHILADELPHIA 1996


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


456 Pa. Super. 148; 689 A.2d 957; 1997 Pa. Super. LEXIS 343


June 25, 1996, Argued  
February 24, 1997, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] The Name of this Case has been Corrected by the Court April 8, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Order dated January 3, 1996 docketed January 4, 1996 in the Court of Common Pleas of Montgomery County, Civil Division, at No. 89-120003. Before SALUS, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order from the Court of Common Pleas of Montgomery County (Pennsylvania) that denied its petition for relief from a judgment of non pros after appellant failed to establish a reasonable explanation for its inactivity in prosecuting its action for breach of contract and tortious interference with contract.


OVERVIEW: After appellant filed a complaint against appellees alleging breach of contract and tortious interference with contract, the trial court granted appellees' motion for a judgment non pros because appellant was unable to establish a reasonable explanation or legitimate excuse for not moving its case forward. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in concluding that appellant was unable to satisfy the necessary elements for opening a judgment of non pros under Pa. R. Civ. P. 3051(b). The court found that all three prongs of the test for a proper judgment of non pros had been met: appellant offered no reason for the delay in process, appellant was unable to prove that it acted with due diligence, and there was an unexplained period of docket inactivity in excess of two years leading to the presumption of prejudice to appellees that was not rebutted by a show of lack of actual prejudice. The court found that the presumption of prejudice could only be rebutted by activity on the docket, and the trial court was not required to consider discover activity off the docket in determining if there was any indication of movement in the case.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order that denied appellant's petition for relief from a judgment of non pros because appellant offered no reason for the delay in process, appellant was unable to prove that it acted with due diligence, and there was an unexplained period of docket inactivity in excess of two years leading to the presumption of prejudice to appellees that was not rebutted by a show of lack of actual prejudice.

DISPOSITION: Judgment of sentence vacated, conviction reversed and Appellant discharged.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review from a judgment of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County (Pennsylvania), convicting him of driving under the influence and various traffic offenses and sentencing him to 30-60 days imprisonment, 23 months probation, and $ 700 in fines.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was stopped by deputy constables after they observed appellant's truck hit a snow bank twice and swerve in front of a bus. The deputy constables arrested appellant and called the city police who then administered a test to check appellant's blood alcohol content levels. Appellant was convicted of driving under the influence and various traffic offenses and sentenced to 30-60 days imprisonment, 23 months probation, and $ 700 in fines. Appellant argued on appeal that his arrest was illegal because the deputy constables lacked the authority to arrest him for traffic violations, the arrest was outside the deputy constables' jurisdiction, and the deputy constables lacked either reasonable suspicion or probable cause to stop him. The court vacated the judgment of sentence, reversed the conviction and discharged appellant. The court held that the deputy constables did not have the authority to arrest appellant for violating the Motor Vehicle Code thus appellant's arrest was invalid. Deputy constables possessed no common law police powers and lacked the training and supervision of police officers and deputy sheriffs to be entrusted with such work.


OUTCOME: The judgment of sentence was vacated, the conviction for driving under the influence and various traffic offenses was reversed and appellant was discharged. Appellant's arrest was invalid because the deputy constable did not have the authority to arrest him for violating the Motor Vehicle Code.

Commonwealth v. Robertson

456 Pa. Super. 209; 690 A.2d 254; 1997 Pa. Super. LEXIS 221

January 29, 1997, FILED

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Court of Common Pleas of York County (Pennsylvania), convicting him of driving under the influence of alcohol and sentencing him as a repeat offender.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found guilty of driving under the influence of alcohol. Commonwealth v. Miller


No. 00435 Harrisburg 1966


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


455 Pa. Super. 534; 689 A.2d 238; 1997 Pa. Super. LEXIS 28


November 12, 1996, Submitted  
January 16, 1997, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Substituted March 21, 1997. Petition for Allowance of Appeal Denied June 25, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Pa. LEXIS 1257.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the JUDGMENT OF SENTENCE April 26, 1996, Docketed April 30, 1996, in the Court of Common Pleas of CENTRE County, CRIMINAL, No. 1996-601. Before, BROWN, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of sentence affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Court of Common Pleas of Centre County (Pennsylvania), which convicted defendant of indirect criminal contempt for harassing and/or stalking his former girlfriend in violation of a protection of abuse order placed against defendant.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's former girlfriend had a protection from abuse order in place against defendant. One day the victim observed defendant following her on his motorcycle. The victim called the police, defendant was told to stay away from the victim, but he drove by her again. Defendant was convicted of indirect criminal contempt for stalking and/or harassing the victim in violation of 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 2709. The appellate court affirmed. The sufficiency of the evidence supported the judgment. The appellate court could not reweigh the evidence and test whether defendant's actions lacked the required intent. The statute could sustain a conviction where defendant merely intended to harass or annoy. The fact that defendant did not physically harm the victim was of no import. Defendant may have had a chance encounter with the victim once, but wherein he made contact five times supported the judgment. There was no constitutional right to travel within the county. That right applied to travel to another state. Section 2709 was not overly broad or vague because it clearly laid out the elements of the crime and the required criminal intent.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction for indirect criminal contempt for stalking and/or harassing the victim was affirmed. The trial court could not reweigh his testimony that he lacked the required intent. Intent was established by intent to harass or annoy, not intent to harm. Defendant's encounter with the victim five times in the same day established intent. The stalking statute was not unconstitutionally vague or overly broad.

Commonwealth v. Highhawk


No. 00220 Pittsburgh 1996


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


455 Pa. Super. 186; 687 A.2d 1123; 1996 Pa. Super. LEXIS 4062


October 1, 1996, Argued  
December 16, 1996, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Application for Reargument Denied February 19, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the ORDER ENTERED January 5, 1996, in the Court of Common Pleas of WESTMORELAND County, CRIMINAL, No. 2407 C 1995. Before CARUSO, J.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The prosecution appealed the judgment of the Court of Common Pleas of Westmoreland County, Pennsylvania, which ordered that the charges against defendant be quashed unless the information was amended to charge a crime because the statute under which defendant was charged, 18 P.S. § 2506, was a sentencing statute and did not create a substantive crime.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with drug delivery resulting in death. Defendant filed a motion to quash the information, and the trial court entered an order stating that the information would be quashed unless it was amended to charge a crime. The prosecution appealed the trial court's judgment, and argued that 18 P.S. § 2506, did define a substantive crime. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment. The court determined that the statute was ambiguous as to whether it meant to create a substantive crime or a sentencing enhancement to other crimes. The court reviewed the legislative history, and held that the legislature had intended to create a substantive crime. The court held that the statute was void for vagueness because the statute's contradictions caused it to fail to give fair notice of the prohibited conduct, in violation of the due process clause of U.S. Const. amend. XIV.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment. The court held that the statute was ambiguous on its face. The court determined that the legislature had meant to create a substantive crime; however, the statute was void for vagueness because it failed to give fair notice of the crime charged.

State of the Art Medical Prods. v. Aries Medical


NO. 244 PHILADELPHIA 1996


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


1996 Pa. Super. LEXIS 3784



December 13, 1996, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Appeal from the Order dated January 3, 1996 docketed January 4, 1996 in the Court of Common Pleas of Montgomery County, Civil Division, at No. 89-120003.



DISPOSITION: The trial court's order is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant company sought review of an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Montgomery County (Pennsylvania), which denied its petition under Pa. R. Civ. P. 3051(b) for relief from a judgment of non pros in its suit against appellees, multiple companies and associations, for breach of contract and tortious interference with contract.


OVERVIEW: Appellant company filed suit against appellees, multiple companies and associations, for breach of contract and tortious interference with contract. After a period in excess of two years in which no docket entries were made, appellees filed a joint motion for judgment of non pros, which the trial court granted. Appellant filed a petition for relief from judgment of non pros, which was denied on the ground that appellant had failed to meet the second prong of the test under Pa. R. Civ. P. 3051(b) by failing to establish a reasonable explanation for the inactivity. The court affirmed and held that the trial court had properly presumed that the delay was prejudicial. Although appellant pointed to non-docketed discovery activity, the court held that prejudice could be presumed if there was no evidence of docketed activity for a period in excess of two years. The court recognized that a trial court could still consider the other prongs of the test for granting of a non pros, whether there was a compelling reason for the delay and whether there was an absence of due diligence in the prosecution, but held that the party responsible for delay could not negate the presumption of prejudice.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order, which denied appellant company's petition for relief from a judgment of non pros. Because appellant failed to establish that there was a reasonable explanation or legitimate excuse for the inactivity on the docket, it was unable to satisfy the necessary elements for opening a judgment of non pros, and so the trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying the relief.

Commonwealth v. Michuck


No. 02169 Pittsburgh 1995


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


454 Pa. Super. 594; 686 A.2d 403; 1996 Pa. Super. LEXIS 3793


May 22, 1996, Argued  
November 19, 1996, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Allowance of Appeal Denied July 11, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence of May 16, 1995 in the Court of Common Pleas, Criminal Division, Cameron County, No. 93-46. Before DAGHIR, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; vacated in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Court of Common Pleas, Criminal Division, Cameron County (Pennsylvania), which entered a judgment of conviction of driving under the influence, in violation of 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. §§ 3731(a)(5)(i), 3731(a)(1). The trial court permitted the admission of blood alcohol test results that were made with blood serum and which applied a middle range conversion factor.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of driving under the influence to a degree rendering one incapable of safe driving, under 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 3731(a)(1) and driving while blood alcohol content was above .10 percent within three hours after driving, under 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 3731(a)(5)(i). The court affirmed the conviction under § 3731(a)(1) because the blood alcohol tests were neither unfair nor arbitrary. The court found that the testing with blood serum and the use of a middle range conversion factor properly complied with acceptable standards, and the admission of this evidence did not cause a verdict against the weight of the evidence. The court reversed the conviction under § 3731(a)(5)(i) because the statute was found unconstitutional as vague and overbroad and thus required the conviction to be vacated. The court found no abuse of discretion in the trial court's refusal to strike a juror for cause who was allegedly within the arresting officer's chain of command because defendant failed to include relevant portions of the record for the court's review of the claim and failed to provide an alternative to a transcript, as provided under Pa. R. App. P. 1923.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of conviction in part because the blood alcohol testing was neither arbitrary nor unfair. The court however reversed the conviction for driving while blood alcohol content is above .10 percent within three hours after driving because that statute had been found unconstitutional due to its vagueness and overbreadth. The court therefore found that the conviction under that statute must be vacated.

Commonwealth v. Hendrickson


No. 407 Pittsburgh 1995, No. 408 Pittsburgh 1995, No. 409 Pittsburgh 1995


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


453 Pa. Super. 533; 684 A.2d 171; 1996 Pa. Super. LEXIS 3546


April 17, 1996, Argued  
October 15, 1996, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence, September 27, 1994, in the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County, Criminal Division, No. CC92-04507, 92-05037. Before DAUER, J.

Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence, September 27, 1994, in the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County, Criminal Division, No. CC 92-04515. Before DAUER, J.

Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence, September 27, 1994, in the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County, Criminal Division, No. CC NO. 92-03772. Before DAUER, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County (Pennsylvania), in which he was convicted of harassment by communication or address pursuant to 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 5504(a)(2). Defendant contended that the statute was unconstitutionally vague and overbroad in violation of U.S. Const. amends. I and XIV, and contested the jurisdiction of the district attorney.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of harassment by communication or address pursuant to 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 5504(a)(2). Defendant sent racially offensive faxes to prominent individuals and civil rights groups. He argued that the statute was unconstitutionally vague and overbroad in violation of U.S. Const. amends. I and XIV, and Pa. Const. art. I, § 7. Defendant also contested the jurisdiction of the district attorney to bring charges against him. The court affirmed the judgment of sentence against defendant. The court found that the statute was not unconstitutionally vague because it contained a requirement that defendant's speech have the specific intent to harass. The court found that defendant's rights under U.S. Const. amend. I were not violated because the state had a legitimate interest in protecting its citizens from harassment and this type of speech did not fall within the core dialogue and free exchange of ideas that U.S. Const. amend. I was designed to protect. The court held that the district attorney did have jurisdiction to prosecute defendant because the faxes were sent into the jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The judgment of sentence for harassment by communication or address against defendant was affirmed. The court held that the statute prohibiting harassment by communication or address was not unconstitutionally vague or overbroad. The court also found that the district attorney had jurisdiction to bring charges against defendant.

Commonwealth v. Tizer


NO. 03665 PHILADELPHIA 1995


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


454 Pa. Super. 1; 684 A.2d 597; 1996 Pa. Super. LEXIS 3409



October 10, 1996, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence September 28, 1995 In the Court of Common Pleas of Bucks County, Criminal Division, No. 793/1995.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of sentence vacated. Case remanded for proceedings consistent with this opinion; trial court is directed to reevaluate appellant's competency at the time of trial. Jurisdiction is not retained.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order from the Court of Common Pleas of Bucks County (Pennsylvania) that entered a judgment of sentence after he was found competent to stand trial and a jury convicted him of terroristic threats under 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. §2706.


OVERVIEW: Appellant threatened to kill his brother after accusing him of conspiring to prevent his access to a trust fund that did, in reality, not exist. The trial court ordered a mental health evaluation of appellant, and it was found that he was competent to stand trial. A jury convicted him of terroristic threats under 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 2706, and on appeal, the court vacated. The court held that based upon the evidence, the trial court could have determined that the commonwealth had established all the elements of the crime of terroristic threats beyond a reasonable doubt. However, the trial court erred in applying the clear and convincing standard to the competency issue when the preponderance of the evidence standard under 50 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 7403 should have been applied retroactively to this case. Appellant was entitled to a remand to allow the trial court to reevaluate his competency to stand trial under the lesser burden. The court concluded that the trial court had not erred in allowing appellant to absent himself from part of his trial because his waiver was not unknowing or involuntary.


OUTCOME: The court vacated appellant's conviction for terroristic threats after he was found competent to stand trial because the trial court erred in applying the clear and convincing standard to the competency issue when the preponderance of the evidence standard should have been applied retroactively. The case was remanded and the trial court was directed to reevaluate appellant's competency under the proper standard.

 

263 of 892 DOCUMENTS


Simmers v. Packer


NO. 00433 HARRISBURG 1995


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


451 Pa. Super. 555; 680 A.2d 904; 1996 Pa. Super. LEXIS 2511


June 12, 1996, Argued  
July 31, 1996, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order entered May 11, 1995 in the Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County, Civil, No. 2443 DR 1993. Before HOOVER, J.



DISPOSITION: The order of the court of Common Pleas vacating the award of child support is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother challenged an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County (Pennsylvania), which ordered her to pay support arrearages and uninsured medical and dental costs, pursuant to 23 P.S. § 4327(a). Appellant's daughter by appellee father was a college student.


OVERVIEW: Appellant mother and appellee father were divorced, and appellant was ordered to pay child support. The daughter had received an $ 8,000 fund from her grandmother for college expenses. Pursuant to 23 P.S. § 4327(a), appellant was ordered to pay a certain portion of the college expenses; she fell into arrears. A lawsuit followed, and appellant was ordered to continue the payments and pay the arrearage. While the appeal was pending, § 4327(a) was declared unconstitutional. On appeal, the court affirmed the child support award because retrospective application of the rule was a matter of judicial discretion to be exercised on a case by case basis. The court reasoned that blanket retroactive application would involve repayment of funds advanced under the unconstitutional statute and would unfairly encumber children of broken families with obligations not borne by children of intact families, as § 4327(a) did not apply to children of intact families; therefore, retroactive application would be violative of equal protection guaranteed by U. S. Const. amend. XIV.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the award which obligated appellant mother to pay child support while her daughter was in college even though the supporting statute had been declared unconstitutional because retroactive application of the new rule would place an unfair burden on children of broken families, who might be obligated to repay funds advanced pursuant to the statute.

Commonwealth v. Ahlborn


NO. 00601 PITTSBURGH, 1995, NO. 01946 PHILADELPHIA, 1994


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


453 Pa. Super. 124; 683 A.2d 632; 1996 Pa. Super. LEXIS 2512


February 26, 1996, Argued  
July 31, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Revised November 14, 1996. Petitions for Allowance of Appeal Granted (NO. 00601 PITTSBURGH, 1995) January 15, 1997. Petitions for Allowance of Appeal Granted ( NO. 01946 PHILADELPHIA, 1994) January 16, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the PCRA Order in the Court of Common Pleas of Westmoreland County, Criminal Division, No. 1148, 1003, 942 & 943, C 1989 C0457214, C0433635, C2587771. Before CARUSO, J. & PAPALINI, J.

Appeal from the PCRA Order in the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, Criminal Division, No. OCTOBER TERM, 1988 NO. 1320-1322. Before CARUSO, J. & PAPALINI, J.

Appeal from the PCRA Order in the Court of Common Pleas, Criminal Division, Westmoreland County, No. 1148, 1103, 942 & 943, C 1989 C0457214, C0433635, C2587771. Before CARUSO, J. & PAPALINI, J.

Appeal from the PCRA Order in the Court of Common Pleas, Criminal Division, Philadelphia County No. October Term, 1988, No. 1320-1322.

Appeal from the Post Conf Relief Act entered June 8, 1994 docketed June 9, 1994 in the Court of Common Pleas of Westmoreland County, Criminal Division, at No. 1148, 1003, 942 & 943 C 1989, C0457214, C0433635, C2587771. Before CARUSO, J. & PAPALINI, J.

Appeal from the Post Conv Relief Act entered May 18, 1994 in the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, Criminal Division, at No. October Term, 1988 No. 1320-1322. Before CARUSO, J. & PAPALINI, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants sought review of orders by Philadelphia Courts of Common Pleas (Pennsylvania), which denied them relief under the Post Conviction Relief Act (PCRA), 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 9541 et seq. The commonwealth contended that appellants were ineligible for PCRA relief because neither appellant was currently serving a sentence of imprisonment, probation, or parole and that their petitions were therefore moot.


OVERVIEW: Appellants were denied relief under the Post Conviction Relief Act (PCRA), 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 9541 et seq. The court affirmed the orders of the lower courts. In order to make its decision, the court had to interpret the language of the statute, which granted eligibility for relief to a person currently serving a sentence of imprisonment, probation, or parole. The court held that the "currently serving" language within PCRA § 9543(a)(1)(i) referred to the time the petition for relief under the statute was filed rather than the time the petition was ultimately adjudicated. The court stated that its conclusion that the "currently serving" requirement necessary for jurisdiction was to be determined at the time the petition was filed did not preclude the possibility that the petition could thereafter become moot. The court then held that appellants' petitions were moot. The court held that upon unconditional release from custody, all cognizable harm necessarily ended and a pending petition, regardless of when it was filed, became moot.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the orders of the lower courts, which denied appellants relief under a post-conviction statute. The court held that even though appellants' petitions were filed prior to their release from custody, they were rendered moot by appellants' subsequent unconditional release.

DiLucido v. Terminix Int'l


NO. 03698 PHILADELPHIA 1995


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


450 Pa. Super. 393; 676 A.2d 1237; 1996 Pa. Super. LEXIS 1617


March 28, 1996, Argued  
May 22, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Allowance of Appeal Denied November 1, 1996, Reported at: 1996 Pa. LEXIS 2125.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Order Dated September 28, 1995 Docketed in the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, Civil, November Term, 1989. No. 597. Before AVELLINO, J.



DISPOSITION: The order of the trial court is hereby affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, consumers, challenged an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), which denied appellants' request for class certification in their action against appellee corporation under the Unfair Trade Practices and Consumer Protection Law.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, consumers, sought class certification in their action against appellee corporation under the Unfair Trade Practices and Consumer Protection Law (UTPCPL). The trial court denied certification because common questions of law or fact did not predominate the case, and appellants' claims were not typical of those asserted for the class. The court affirmed and held that appellants failed to satisfy the typicality requirements for class certification. The court ruled that appellants failed to show that they could proceed under the various sections of the UTPCPL. The court found that appellants failed to present sufficient evidence to establish that their alleged loss was a result of misrepresentations by appellee, as required in a private action under the UTPCPL. Therefore, their claims were not typical of the members of the proposed class.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a decision to deny appellants, consumers', request for class certification because they failed to establish that they could proceed under the Unfair Trade Practices and Consumer Protection Law; they failed to show that their claims were typical of the proposed class.

Commonwealth v. Neitzel


NO. 01344 PHILADELPHIA 1995


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


451 Pa. Super. 1; 678 A.2d 369; 1996 Pa. Super. LEXIS 1219


February 8, 1996, Argued  
May 21, 1996, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence Entered March 8, 1995 In the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, Criminal Division No. 949-15024, M.R. # 949-15025. Before ALLEN, J.

Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence Entered March 8, 1995 in the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, Criminal Division No. 949-15024, M.R. # 949-15024. Before ALLEN, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of sentence affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment entered in the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, Criminal Division (Pennsylvania), which found him guilty of violating game tag regulations under 34 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 2103, 16 U.S.C.S. §§ 703-712, and 50 C.F.R. §§ 20.26, 20.37 relating to his possession of a Merganser hen and a Wood Duck.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's taxidermy shop was raided by the Pennsylvania Game Commission and the U.S. Fish and Wildlife Service, who found two frozen, untagged, migratory game bird carcasses. The carcasses were seized and defendant was arrested for violations of 34 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 2103, 16 U.S.C.S. §§ 703-712, and 50 C.F.R. §§ 20.26, 20.37. He was found guilty as charged in Philadelphia Municipal Court and appealed for a trial de novo in the Court of Common Pleas. The trial court found defendant guilty of two violations of 34 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 2103 and fined him $ 100 for each bird. Defendant appealed and argued that he could not be convicted of an offense for which he was not properly charged, and the trial court erred in amending the charges filed. The court affirmed and held that the citation given defendant which referenced the key statutory sections he had violated provided defendant fair and adequate notice of the crimes charged and defendant was not prejudiced in any way.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for violation of Pennsylvania game laws and held that the citation provided defendant fair and adequate notice of the charges against him.

Commonwealth v. Taylor


NO. 00702 PITTSBURGH, 1995


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


450 Pa. Super. 583; 677 A.2d 846; 1996 Pa. Super. LEXIS 1204


January 9, 1996, Submitted  
May 7, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended on Grant of Partial Reconsideration June 24, 1996, Reported at: 1996 Pa. Super. LEXIS 2122.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Suppression Order in the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County, Criminal Division, No. 9111463. Before LITTLE, J.



DISPOSITION: Case remanded for proceedings consistent with this Opinion. Jurisdiction relinquished.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant commonwealth challenged an order from the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County (Pennsylvania) granting appellee's motion to suppress cocaine recovered during a warrantless arrest and search by a constable.


OVERVIEW: While a constable was in appellee's apartment to evict him for failure to pay rent, he noticed a plastic bag of a white substance and a large sum of prepackaged money. The constable then arrested appellee and conducted a search of his person, finding numerous bags containing what he thought was an illegal drug. Appellee pled guilty to possession of a controlled substance and possession with intent to deliver but was granted the right to withdraw that plea. The trial court granted appellee's motion to suppress the cocaine after finding that the constable lacked the authority to arrest appellee. On appeal, the court remanded, holding that the constable possessed the common law power to make a warrantless arrest for felony drug law violations. The court found no statutory provision abrogating that power, and since appellee's possession of a controlled substance with intent to deliver constituted a felony under 35 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 780-113(f)(1), the constable was empowered to make the arrest. However, the fact that the constable had the power to arrest did not make the arrest legal unless probable cause existed. Thus, the court remanded for a determination of probable cause.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the case for a finding of probable cause after determining that a constable had the common law authority to arrest appellee for possession and possession with intent to deliver an illegal drug and that the trial court had erred in granting appellee's motion to suppress cocaine.

Commonwealth v. Fowlin


No. 633 Philadelphia 1995


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


450 Pa. Super. 489; 676 A.2d 665; 1996 Pa. Super. LEXIS 924


November 2, 1995, Argued  
April 12, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected July 12, 1996. Petition for Allowance of Appeal Granted December 10, 1996, Reported at: 1996 Pa. LEXIS 2459.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the ORDER of October 19, 1994 in the Court of Common Pleas, Criminal Division, Northampton County, at No. 282-1984. Before FRANCIOSA, J.

Appeal from Order of the Court of Common Pleas, Criminal Division, of Northampton County, No. 282-1984. Before FRANCIOSA, J.

Appeal from the Order entered October 19, 1994 in the Court of Common Pleas of Northampton County, Criminal Division, at No. 282-1984. Before FRANCIOSA, J.

Appeal from the Order of October 19, 1994 in the Court of Common Pleas of Northampton County, Criminal Division, No. 282-1984. Before FRANCIOSA, J.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed. Case remanded for trial. Jurisdiction relinquished.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from the Court of Common Pleas, Northampton County (Pennsylvania), which denied appellant's petition for habeas corpus relief and concluded that appellant could be held criminally culpable even though he acted in justifiable self-defense.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was charged with various offenses stemming from shootings in which appellant injured a bystander. The trial court denied appellant's petition for habeas corpus and concluded that appellant could be held criminally culpable. On appeal, the court held that where an actor was justified in using force upon or toward another person, but recklessly or negligently injured or killed an innocent person, the justification afforded the actor is unavailable, in a prosecution based upon reckless or negligent conduct towards the innocent person. The court found that because appellant acted in lawful self-defense and did not possess a purposeful or knowing mental state towards his attackers, the state was precluded from pursuing a charge based on an intentional or knowing infliction of serious bodily injury. However, the court continued that there was sufficient evidence to make out a prima facie case with regard to the to the injuries to the innocent bystander caused by the reckless or negligent acts of appellant. The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court and remanded the case for trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court denying the petition for habeas corpus and remanded the case for trial because a person acting in lawful self-defense, who recklessly or negligently injures an innocent bystander, could be held criminally culpable for the injuries inflicted upon the bystander.

Commonwealth v. Gayle


No. 00518 Harrisburg 1995


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


449 Pa. Super. 247; 673 A.2d 927; 1996 Pa. Super. LEXIS 335


December 11, 1995, Argued  
March 13, 1996, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence of the Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County, Criminal Division at No. 1858 CD 1994. Before KLEINFELTER, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of sentence is vacated and this case is reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from the Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County (Pennsylvania), which convicted appellant of possession with intent to distribute, possession of marihuana, and possession of drug paraphernalia.


OVERVIEW: The court vacated the judgment, reversed, and remanded the case for a new trial because it found that the lower court failed to suppress illegally seized evidence. The court found that appellant, as a parolee, did not have a diminished expectation of privacy under U.S. Const. amend. IV and Pa. Const. art. I, § 8. The court found that appellant was stopped by the police for a faulty headlight and that parole officers had instructed the police to hold appellant until they could search him. The court found that the initial stop by the police was proper, but that the continued detention of appellant elevated to an investigatory stop for which the officers needed an articulable and reasonable basis. The court held that the officers did not have reasonable suspicion based on the fact that appellant had a pager and was present in a high crime area. The court concluded that there was no reasonable basis to suspect appellant was connected with any criminal activity and the search of appellant's person was the product of an illegal detention. The court held that the evidence seized from appellant's person should have been suppressed because it was fruit of the poisonous tree.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the judgment, reversed, and remanded the case because it found that the lower court failed to suppress evidence that had been seized during an illegal detention and that the evidence was fruit of the poisonous tree.

Commonwealth v. Balog


No. 836 Pittsburgh, 1995


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


448 Pa. Super. 480; 672 A.2d 319; 1996 Pa. Super. LEXIS 237


August 14, 1995, Submitted  
February 13, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Allowance of Appeal Denied August 1, 1996. Certiorari Denied February 18, 1997, Reported at: 1997 U.S. LEXIS 993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence entered April 5, 1995, Court of Common Pleas, Greene County, Criminal Division at No. 335, 1994. Before GRIMES, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Court of Common Pleas, Greene County (Pennsylvania), finding him guilty of cruelty to animals (gamecocks) under 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 5511(h.1)(3) and sentencing him to 54 months probation, a $ 1,000 fine, and ordering him to pay restitution.


OVERVIEW: Appealing his conviction for cruelty to animals (gamecocks), defendant argued that 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 5511(h.1)(3), which prohibited owning animals for animal fighting, was vague and overbroad in violation of U.S. Const. amend. I and XIV. He also argued that his conduct fell within a statutory exception to the crime of cruelty to animals and that a humane society officer that testified at trial was not qualified as an expert. On appeal, the court affirmed the sentence. The court held that defendant failed to carry his burden of showing that the statute was unconstitutional. The court held that defendant's conduct fell within the scope of the statute. The court found that a trooper with a search warrant discovered individually caged roosters altered for fighting on defendant's property and that he seized 36 magazines on fighting birds and two sets of spurs. The agent that testified as an expert participated in about 100 investigations involving cockfighting and qualified as an expert on the subject in 20 court cases. Thus, the trial court did not abuse its discretion in admitting his testimony.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of cruelty to animals (gamecocks) and the sentence imposed by the trial court. The court held that defendant did not show that the statute was unconstitutionally overbroad and found that defendant's conduct was prohibited by the statute.

 

271 of 892 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. McIvor


No. 1074 Philadelphia 1995


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


448 Pa. Super. 98; 670 A.2d 697; 1996 Pa. Super. LEXIS 116


September 11, 1995, Argued  
January 22, 1996, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Allowance of Appeal Denied March 5, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Pa. LEXIS 464.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Order, November 7, 1994, in the Court of Common Pleas of Chester County, Criminal Division, No. 2014-94. Before MELODY, J.

Appeal from the Order in the Court of Common Pleas of Chester County, Criminal Division, No. 2014-94. Before MELODY, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of an order from the Court of Common Pleas of Chester County, Criminal Division (Pennsylvania), which denied his petition for writ of habeas corpus in connection with appellant's conviction and accompanying sentence for three violations of the Wiretapping and Electronic Surveillance Control Act, 19 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 5701 et. seq.


OVERVIEW: On review, appellant contended that his conduct had not violated the Wiretapping and Electronic Surveillance Control Act (Act), 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 5701 et. seq., because none of appellant's conversations with the stopped motorists constituted an "oral communication" as defined under the Act. The court noted that the definition of "original communication" required a specific expectation of non-interception, justified under the circumstances, in order to bring the communication within the ambit of the Act. The court then found that under the circumstances of the instant case, while the stopped motorists had no expectation of privacy with respect to appellant, the police officer who had stopped them, the motorists had a very real expectation of non-interception. The court accordingly held that intercepts conducted by appellant constituted oral communications within the meaning of the Act. The court affirmed, rejecting appellant's assertion that his participant monitoring had been legal under the exception contained in 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 5704(2)(i) where appellant had failed to obtain the requisite approval and supervisor prior to making the intercepts in question.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of the petition for writ of habeas corpus, finding that intercepts of the stopped motorists' statements qualified as "oral communications" under the Wiretapping and Electronic Surveillance Control Act (Act) where the motorists had a justifiable expectation of non-interception during the traffic stop. Appellant's monitoring was not exempt under the Act where he failed to obtain the requisite approval and supervision.

Allen by Allen v. Montgomery Hosp.


No. 3129 Philadelphia 1994


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


447 Pa. Super. 158; 668 A.2d 565; 1995 Pa. Super. LEXIS 3697


May 18, 1995, Argued  
December 19, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Allowance of Appeal Granted May 29, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Order entered August 18, 1994, Court of Common Pleas, Montgomery County, Civil Division at No. 83-16964. Before NICHOLAS, J.
Allen v. Montgomery Hosp., 22 Pa. D. & C.4th 150, 1994 Pa. Dist. & Cnty. Dec. LEXIS 110 (1994)



DISPOSITION: Order Reversed. Case Remanded. Jurisdiction Relinquished.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, an incompetent and her guardian parents, challenged an order of the Court of Common Pleas, Montgomery County, (Pennsylvania), Civil Division. The question on appeal was whether the immunity provision of the Mental Health Procedures Act applied to a health care provider who was not trained in the field of mental health, and who treated a patient's physical ailments, not a mental illness.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, an incompetent daughter and her parents, sought review of a trial court order that denied their motion for a new trial and entered judgment for appellee hospital and appellee physician. Appellant daughter was diagnosed as mentally retarded with psychosis after an adverse reaction to medication and also suffered physical ailments, including fever, dehydration, and a possible urinary tract infection. Appellants brought suit against the appellees to recover for appellant daughter's injuries and for derivative claims. Appellees filed a joint motion in limine requesting a ruling as to whether the Mental Health Procedures Act (MHPA), 50 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 7101, et seq., was controlling contending the MHPA afforded them limited immunity absent willful misconduct or gross negligence. The trial court granted the motion. Appellant sought review on interlocutory appeal which was denied, then pursued appeal after denial of a new trial motion. Concluding that adequate treatment with the least restrictive alternatives was the hallmark of the MHPA, the court concluded the immunity provision applied to appellees. The court reversed the trial court judgment and remanded for a new trial.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court judgment for appellee physician and appellee hospital. The court found the immunity provision of the Mental Health Procedures Act did apply to the appellees in a situation where they had provided non-psychiatric care to appellant daughter, a patient who had been diagnosed with mental health and physical health ailments. The court remanded the case back for a new trial.

Croatian Roman Catholic Congregation of the Holy Trinity Church v. Wuerl


NO. 122 PITTSBURGH 1995, NO. 254 PITTSBURGH 1995, NO. 733 PITTSBURGH 1995


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


447 Pa. Super. 208; 668 A.2d 1151; 1995 Pa. Super. LEXIS 3689


September 27, 1995, Argued  
December 18, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petitions for Allowance of Appeal Denied September 11, 1996. Certiorari Denied February 18, 1997, Reported at: 1997 U.S. LEXIS 782.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Order Entered December 14, 1994, in the Court of Common Pleas of Beaver County, Civil Division, at No. 10479 of 1994. Before KUNSELMAN & STRANAHAN, JJ.

Appeal from the Order Entered January 10, 1995, in the Court of Common Pleas of Lawrence County, Civil Division, at No. 460 of 1993 CA. Before KUNSELMAN & STRANAHAN, JJ.

Appeal from the Order Entered March 27, 1995, in the Court of Common Pleas of Beaver County, Civil Division, at No. 11190 of 1994. Before KUNSELMAN & STRANAHAN, JJ.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a consolidated appeal, appellants sought review of the orders from the Court of Common Pleas of Beaver County (Pennsylvania), and the Court of Common Pleas of Lawrence County (Pennsylvania), which dismissed for lack of standing, appellants' suit against appellee, which challenged appellee's suppression of appellants' parishes.


OVERVIEW: Appellants were congregations of Roman Catholic churches whose parishes were suppressed by appellee. Appellants then sued appellee, and the cases were dismissed in the trial courts for appellants' lack of standing. The appeals filed by appellants were consolidated. Appellants asserted that the trial courts erred in determining that they did not have standing to pursue their cases. The court held that under the church law, the effect of dismemberment was to cause the parish to cease to exist and to transfer its members to adjoining parishes. Dismemberment also deprived parish's members of all rights as members in the church property of the parish from which they were transferred. Finally, division, dismemberment, or suppression of parishes, and the effect thereof on membership were purely ecclesiastical matters, and the court did not review the merits of a decision rendered in an ecclesiastical matter by the appropriate church tribunal or official. Accordingly, the orders of the trial courts were affirmed.


OUTCOME: Orders of dismissal of appellants' suits against appellee affirmed where because appellants sought review of the suppression of their parishes, which were purely ecclesiastical matters, the trial courts would not review those matters.
