Commonwealth v. Metts


No. 00442 Pittsburgh 1994


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


447 Pa. Super. 275; 669 A.2d 346; 1995 Pa. Super. LEXIS 3681


September 11, 1995, Argued  
December 6, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Allowance of Appeal Granted May 29, 1996, Reported at: 1996 Pa. LEXIS 1142.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence in the Court of Common Pleas of Fayette County, Criminal Division, at Nos. 769, 769 2/6, 769 3/6, 769 4/6 of 1992. Before WAGNER, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgments of sentence affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Fayette County (Pennsylvania), which convicted him of first degree murder, robbery, theft by unlawful taking or disposition, and receiving stolen property.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of first degree murder, robbery, theft by unlawful taking or disposition, and receiving stolen property. Appellant's friend cooperated with police and wore an electronic transmitter while questioning appellant about his involvement in the murder. At trial, an excerpt from the tape, wherein appellant confessed to shooting the victim, was admitted into evidence. Appellant claimed that a recent Pa. Supreme Court decision that held that the Wiretapping and Electronic Surveillance Control Act (Wiretap Act), 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 5701 et seq., was unconstitutional without a showing of probable cause, was applicable, retroactively, to his appeal. The court affirmed, holding that although appellant had standing to assert a Fourth Amendment search and seizure claim, the new rule of law providing for exclusion of evidence resulting from wiretapping without probable cause did not apply. The court held that the weighing of relevant factors supported only a prospective application of the new rule of law, and found no evidence that police failed to comply with the Wiretap Act, or that their conduct was so outrageous as to constitute a violation of due process.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment convicting appellant of first degree murder, robbery, theft by unlawful taking or disposition, and receiving stolen property. The court held that a recent Pa. Supreme Court decision that provided for the exclusion of evidence obtained through the act of wiretapping, when there was no showing of probable cause, was not applicable retroactively to appellant's case.

Commonwealth v. Schierscher

SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA

November 30, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Allowance of Appeal Denied January 21, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Pa. LEXIS 212.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence of the Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County, Criminal Division at No. 678 CD 1994. Before GATES, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of sentence affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of sentence of the Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County (Pennsylvania) for threats and other improper influences in official and political matters, retaliation for past official action, harassment, stalking, harassment by communication or address, and obstruction or impeding the administration of justice by picketing.


OVERVIEW: Defendant engaged in a campaign of leaflet distribution and endless phone calls that denounced and threatened a judge in connection with several cases that were decided against defendant. Defendant was convicted of numerous crimes including harassment, stalking, and obstruction or impeding the administration of justice by picketing, and the court affirmed his conviction. The testimony of three individuals and three judges was irrelevant and inadmissible because their testimony would not have been illuminating on the charges. Defendant's conviction for obstruction or impeding the administration of justice did not violate his constitutional right to demonstrate because his stated purpose was to induce the judge to alter her decisions. Stat. § 2709 because the statute was constitutional and reasonably restricted conduct without being "vague" or "overbroad."


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of sentence for many crimes including harassment, stalking, and obstruction or impeding the administration of justice by picketing. The conviction for obstruction or impeding the administration of justice did not violate defendant's constitutional right to demonstrate because his purpose was to induce a judge to alter her decision in several cases. The statute prohibiting harassment and stalking was constitutional.

Columbia Gas v. Carl E. Baker, Inc.


NO. 00875 HBG 1994, NO. 00876 HBG 1994, NO. 00877 HBG 1994


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


446 Pa. Super. 481; 667 A.2d 404; 1995 Pa. Super. LEXIS 3366


September 20, 1995, Argued  
October 31, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order entered November 21, 1994 docketed November 22, 1994, in the Court of Common Pleas of York County, Civil, No. 92-SU-00100-01. Before ERB, J.

Appeal from the Order entered November 21, 1994 docketed November 22, 1994, in the Court of Common Pleas of York County, Civil, No. 91-SU-00905-01. Before ERB, J.

Appeal from the Order entered November 21, 1994 docketed November 22, 1994, in the Court of Common Pleas of York County, Civil, No. 92-SU-001320-01. Before ERB, J.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant gas company challenged a decision from the Court of Common Pleas of York County (Pennsylvania) that granted appellees, contractor and engineer, judgment on the pleadings in homeowners' action for property damages.


OVERVIEW: Appellee contractor and engineers were hired to design and install sanitary sewers in parts of a city. During the installation of such sewers, appellees struck and damaged gas lines owned and operated by appellant gas company. Eighteen years after installation of the sewer lines, a natural gas explosion occurred and several homes were destroyed. Homeowners initiated an action against appellants and appellees. Appellees were granted judgment on the pleadings because the statute of repose, 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 5536(a), extinguished the homeowners' action. On appeal, the court affirmed the decision. The homeowners did not bring their action against appellees within 12 years of the completion of the installation of the sewer lines, so their action was barred by the statute of repose. The fact that appellant had no control over the installation was irrelevant because appellees' actions fell within the parameters of the statute of repose.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision granting appellees, contractor and engineer, judgment on the pleadings. The 12 year statute of repose barred the homeowners' action against appellees because appellees completed the installation of the sewer lines 18 years before homeowners initiated their action.

Sejpal v. Corson, Mitchell, Tomhave & McKinley, M.D.'s

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant former patient sought review of a decision by the Court of Common Pleas of Cambria County, Civil Division (Pennsylvania), which denied her motion for leave to amend her complaint and granted judgment on the pleadings to appellees, doctors and a hospital.


OVERVIEW: The trial court granted judgment on the pleadings to appellees, doctors and a hospital, in appellant former patient's action for their performance of a sterilization operation on her without her informed consent, holding that the action was based on wrongful birth and thus was barred by 42 Pa. The court remanded the action for further proceedings.

Commonwealth v. Henderson


No. 572 Philadelphia 1994, No. 578 Philadelphia 1994, No. 581 Philadelphia 1994


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


444 Pa. Super. 170; 663 A.2d 728; 1995 Pa. Super. LEXIS 2272


May 10, 1995, Argued  
August 10, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order dated February 1, 1994, in the Court of Common Pleas of Chester County, Criminal, No. 1587-93. Before GAVIN, J.

Appeal from the Order dated February 1, 1994, in the Court of Common Pleas of Chester County, Criminal, No. 2531-93. Before GAVIN, J.

Appeal from the Order dated February 1, 1994, in the Court of Common Pleas of Chester County, Criminal, No. 1841-93. Before GAVIN, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The commonwealth sought review of the judgment of the Court of Common Pleas of Chester County (Pennsylvania), which granted pre-trial motions filed by appellees, motorist and passengers, to suppress evidence which was obtained when the police stopped appellees on a seatbelt violation and subsequently discovered evidence which led to drug possession charges.


OVERVIEW: Appellees, motorist and passengers, were charged with multiple drug-related offenses after their vehicle was stopped by a police officer who noticed that appellees were not wearing seat belts. The trial court granted appellees' pre-trial motions to suppress all statements and physical evidence associated with the case holding that a violation of 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 4581, a law requiring motorists to wear seatbelts, did not provide the officer with probable cause to stop appellees' vehicle. The court affirmed the trial court's suppression order and held that the police were not authorized to stop appellees' vehicle unless they had reasonable and articulable grounds to suspect that the motor vehicle code was being violated. The court held that appellees' non-compliance with § 4581 was not a violation of the motor vehicle code because appellees were not also convicted of simultaneously violating another motor vehicle code provision. The court held that because the police had no reason to stop appellees' vehicle, the stop was illegal, and as such, all evidence accumulated pursuant to the stop constituted "the fruits of a poisonous tree" and was subject to being suppressed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court which granted motions filed by appellees, motorist and passengers, to suppress evidence obtained pursuant to a stop by the police. The court held that the police were not authorized to stop appellees' vehicle because appellees' non-compliance with a seat belt law, in and of itself, did not give the police reasonable and articulable grounds to suspect a violation of the motor vehicle code.

SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence October 5, 1993 in the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County, Criminal Nos. 8308693, 8308694, 8308808, 8308809, 8308810.

Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence, October 5, 1993, in the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County, Criminal Division, No. 8308693, 8308694, 8308808, 8308809, 8308810.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County (Pennsylvania) where appellant was found guilty but mentally ill on two counts of murder of the first degree and three counts of reckless endangerment of another person.


OVERVIEW: Appellant began having auditory hallucinations. Subsequently, appellant was diagnosed a paranoid schizophrenic and was prescribed medication, which he took sporadically. One day, appellant went to the neighbor's home, fired into the group of guests who were outside, killed two of them, and wounded three others. Appellant sought a not guilty verdict based on his insanity defense, however, he was found guilty but mentally ill on two counts of murder of the first degree and three counts of reckless endangerment of another person. OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed because the verdict was not against the weight of the evidence, the verdict of guilty but mentally ill did not deprive appellant of due process and equal protection, and there was no error in the trial court's instructions to the jury.

Commonwealth v. Brehm


No. 00752 Harrisburg 1994


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


444 Pa. Super. 138; 663 A.2d 712; 1995 Pa. Super. LEXIS 2208



August 1, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Allowance of Appeal Granted October 31, 1996, Reported at: 1996 Pa. LEXIS 2136.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence of the Court of Common Pleas of Cumberland County, Criminal Division at No. 1466 CRIMINAL 1993.

Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence October 18, 1994, in the Court of Common Pleas of Cumberland County, Criminal, No. 1466 CRIMINAL 1993.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment of the Court of Common Pleas of Cumberland County (Pennsylvania), convicting him of driving while under the influence of alcohol.


OVERVIEW: Appellant sought review of his conviction for driving under the influence of alcohol under 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 3731(a)(5), contending that the trial court erred by permitting the state to include a charge under § 3731(a)(5) with charges under Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. §§ 3731(a)(1) and (4), and that § 3731(a)(5) violated his due process rights as it was overbroad and lacked a rational relationship to a legitimate state interest. The court affirmed, holding that § 3731(a)(5) was cognate to §§ 3731(a)(1) and 3731(a)(4) and that any deficiency in the presentation of the case in its preliminary stages was harmless once it was determined at trial that the state's evidence was sufficient to be presented to a jury. The court found that § 3731(a)(5) was not overbroad and it reflected the state's legitimate interest in controlling drunk driving; nor did it shift the burden of proof to appellant to show that he had a blood alcohol level above .10 percent within three hours of driving because that was not an element of the offense and the prosecution still had to prove beyond a reasonable doubt that his blood alcohol level was .10 percent or more.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for driving while under the influence of alcohol, holding that the statute under which appellant was charged was not overbroad and reflected a legitimate state interest in controlling drunk driving. Thus, appellant's due process rights were not violated by his conviction.

Commonwealth v. Smith


No. 00222 Pittsburgh 1994


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


444 Pa. Super. 652; 664 A.2d 622; 1995 Pa. Super. LEXIS 1865



July 6, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reargument Denied September 13, 1995. Petition for Allowance of Appeal Denied April 4, 1996, Reported at: 1996 Pa. LEXIS 577. Reconsideration Denied July 12, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence of the Court of Common Pleas, Criminal Division, of Allegheny County at No. CC 92-13814.



DISPOSITION: Vacated, remanded and relinquished.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The commonwealth sought review of a judgment of sentence from the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County, Criminal Division (Pennsylvania), which did not impose the mandatory minimum sentence on appellee due to the commonwealth's previous offer to waive the mandatory sentence during unsuccessful plea negotiations. The commonwealth's motion to reconsider was denied.


OVERVIEW: As part of appellee's plea bargain, the commonwealth agreed that it would not seek any applicable mandatory minimum sentence. Appellee later withdrew his guilty plea and was convicted of possession of a controlled substance with intent to deliver, possession of a controlled substance, criminal conspiracy, and prohibited offensive weapons. The commonwealth intended to proceed under the mandatory sentencing provisions, but the trial court refused to impose the mandatory minimum sentence and denied the commonwealth's motion to reconsider. On appeal, the court vacated the sentence and remanded the case for resentencing. It was within the sole discretion of the commonwealth whether to invoke the mandatory minimum sentence and the trial court was required to follow the law, despite its belief that the law was flawed. The decision whether to enter into plea negotiations was a function of prosecutorial discretion and was not based on an invidious classification. The commonwealth's plea negotiation policy was not unconstitutionally infirm and was not arbitrarily or discriminatorily applied.


OUTCOME: Appellee's judgment of sentence was vacated and the case was remanded for resentencing. The trial court's failure to impose the mandatory minimum sentence was error because it was within the sole discretion of commonwealth to determine whether to seek a mandatory sentence and such discretion could be used in a constitutionally firm manner during plea negotiations.

Commonwealth v. Minnich


NO. 01754 PHILADELPHIA, 1994, NO. 03916 PHILADELPHIA, 1994


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


443 Pa. Super. 472; 662 A.2d 21; 1995 Pa. Super. LEXIS 1762


March 29, 1995, Argued  
June 13, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence in the Court of Common Pleas of Berks County, Criminal Division, No. 3196/93. Before SPRECHER, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Court of Common Pleas, Berks County, Criminal Division (Pennsylvania), sentencing him to two consecutive terms of imprisonment after he pled guilty to two counts of homicide by motor vehicle. Defendant appealed on grounds that multiple sentences imposed as a result of a single criminal act violated his due process and equal protection rights under federal and state constitutions.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled guilty to two counts of homicide by motor vehicle after two of his passengers were killed in a crash. Defendant appealed his sentence of two consecutive terms on grounds that the multiple sentences imposed as a result of a single criminal act violated his due process and equal protection rights under the federal and state constitutions. The court noted that both U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Pa. Const. art. III, § 32 mandated that statutory classifications not implicating fundamental interests or suspect classes had to bear a rational relationship to a legitimate state interest. Defendant did not clearly demonstrate unconstitutionality. The purpose of the homicide by vehicle statute was to reduce highway fatalities. Imposition of consecutive sentences served this purpose, provided punishment proportionate to criminal liability, and punished serious offenders more severely. Defendant also challenged the lower court's imposition of sentence in the aggravated range. Defendant did not properly preserve the issue for review and nevertheless failed to raise the appearance of a substantial question as to the appropriateness of sentence. The judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: Defendant's sentence to two consecutive terms upon his conviction for two counts of homicide by motor vehicle was affirmed. The imposition of multiple sentences as a result of a single criminal act, the car crash which took two lives, did not violate defendant's due process or equal protection rights under the federal and state constitutions. The statute was rationally related to the state's interest to reduce highway fatalities.

Bolton v. Bolton


No. 00964 Philadelphia 1994


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


441 Pa. Super. 482; 657 A.2d 1270; 1995 Pa. Super. LEXIS 989


October 20, 1994, Argued  
April 25, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from ORDER entered February 18, 1994, in the Court of Common Pleas of Carbon County, CIVIL, No. 030788. Before WEBB, J.

Appeal from the Order entered February 18, 1994 in the Court of Common Pleas of Carbon County, Civil No. 030788. Before WEBB, J.



DISPOSITION: Vacated and remanded with instructions. Jurisdiction relinquished.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father sought review of an order by the Court of Common Pleas of Carbon County, Pennsylvania, which dismissed his exceptions and adopted the findings of fact and temporary support order recommended by a hearing officer regarding his son, a recent university graduate.


OVERVIEW: Appellant father was ordered to pay $ 109 per month to help his adult son through college. A court decision handed down a decision outlawing this type of payment, but the legislature enacted 23 Pa. Cons. Stat. §4327 (Act 62) creating a statutory duty for divorced parents to pay for their adult children's college education. The trial court then ordered appellant to pay $ 127, retroactive to the date of the suspension of the prior order. The court vacated and remanded the decision because Act 62 support awards had to be limited to defined educational costs. The court found that support award amount included sundries such as car insurance and cable television and appellant properly excepted to inclusion of personal expenses in the support award. Furthermore, the court held that the educational expenses were not properly documented. The only evidence submitted was one semester's tuition bill and no receipts for other defined education expenses such as books. Lastly, the court held that under Act 62 the guideline amounts, which had been formulated to reflect what parents of a particular income level would reasonable expected to spend in support of their minor children, should be used.


OUTCOME: Trial court's judgment for support of 21-year old son and his educational expenses was vacated and remanded with instructions because support awards had to be limited to defined educational costs, and these educational cost should be carefully documented. The court further held that since the costs had been liquidated, the trial court's order could result in a money judgment, but not a support order.

Commonwealth v. Patosky


NO. 01335 PGH 93


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


440 Pa. Super. 535; 656 A.2d 499; 1995 Pa. Super. LEXIS 589



March 16, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Allowance of Appeal Denied September 19, 1995, Reported at: 1995 Pa. LEXIS 690.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence August 5, 1993 in the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County, Criminal Division, at No. 9102941.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant airline employee challenged a judgment from the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County, Criminal Division (Pennsylvania), which convicted him of indecent assault. Appellant contended that the trial court erred in failing to allow an in-camera review of the alleged victim's psychiatric records, and in erroneously admitting the testimony about appellant's prior "off-color" statements to two witnesses.


OVERVIEW: Appellant airline employee challenged his conviction for indecent assault on a co-worker, contending that the trial court erred in failing to allow an in-camera review of the alleged victim's psychiatric records. Appellant also contended that the trial court erroneously failed to caution the jury, as requested, on the victim's credibility based on her failure to file a prompt complaint. Appellant also argued that the trial court erroneously admitted the testimony of two witnesses regarding appellant's prior "off-color" statements to them. The victim testified that the indecent assault occurred in the break room of the airline's freight dock. The victim's supervisor testified that the victim was the only female working in the air freight division with appellant and was fearful of causing trouble by reporting the incident. The appellate court affirmed conviction because psychiatric records were protected by an absolute statutory privilege and were not subject to disclosure. The appellate court held that although evidence of appellant's reputation was not admissible it became admissible because appellant placed his reputation at issue and opened the door to rebuttal.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction for indecent assault was affirmed because appellant's arguments lacked merit. The court held that appellant's constitutional rights were not violated by denial of access to the victim's statutorily protected psychiatric records. The court also held that appellant himself delved into what would have been objectionable testimony, which entitled appellee state to probe into the objectionable area.

 

287 of 892 DOCUMENTS


Byrnes v. Caldwell


NO. 978 PHILADELPHIA 1994


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


439 Pa. Super. 574; 654 A.2d 1125; 1995 Pa. Super. LEXIS 266



February 9, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Allowance of Appeal Granted May 18, 1995, Reported at: 1995 Pa. LEXIS 2495.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Order Entered February 15, 1994, in the Court of Common Pleas, Civil Division, of Montgomery County, No. 92-20581.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father sought reversal of the order of the Court of Common Pleas of Montgomery County (Pennsylvania), which reopened a petition to support a child in college and imposed a support obligation under Act 62, 23 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 4327. The trial court rejected appellant's claims that the statute was unconstitutional under the federal and state constitutions as an ex post facto law and as a violation of equal protection.


OVERVIEW: Appellant father was ordered to pay support for a child in college after the trial court reconsidered a support petition that had been denied under recent decisional law, that was promptly reversed by the legislature through the enactment of 23 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 4327 (Act 62). Act 62 retroactively reinstated prior decisional law. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that appellant had not shown either undue hardship or estrangement that would effect his support obligation. The court held that Act 62 was not penal, so it was not an ex post facto law under U.S. Const. art. I, § 10, cl. 1 or Pa. Const. art. I, § 1. The court considered appellant's equal protection claims under U.S. Const. amend. XIV, § 1 and Pa. Const. art. I, § 1 and art. III, § 32, under the restraint that review of equal protection was not a license for courts to judge the wisdom, fairness, or logic of legislative choices. The court found that appellant did not show that he was in a suspect or sensitive class. The court applied a rational basis test and found that the legislature had a rational basis for classifying divorced parents differently from parents in intact families, so Act 62 was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court, which held that appellant father had a duty to support his daughter in college because Act 62 was constitutional. The court held Act 62 was not penal and, therefore, not ex post facto, and it did not deny equal protection because the legislature had a rational basis creating a classification of divorced parents.

Commonwealth v. Urrutia


NO. 00164 HARRISBURG 1994


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


439 Pa. Super. 227; 653 A.2d 706; 1995 Pa. Super. LEXIS 124



January 27, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Judgment Entered March 14, 1994, In the Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County, CRIMINAL, No. 2333 CD 1993.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County (Pennsylvania), that entered a judgment of sentence against defendant after a jury convicted him of stalking.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of stalking pursuant to Pennsylvania's stalking law, 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 2709(b). Defendant appealed the judgment of sentence and asserted that evidence of two prior violent acts perpetrated against the victim were inadmissible as prior bad acts. On appeal, the court held that defendant was properly convicted of stalking and that evidence of the two prior related violent acts were admissible because they fit under the exceptions to the general rule of inadmissibility. In the instant case, the prior bad acts showed defendant's intent and course of conduct, which was also admissible as an element of the crime of stalking. The court also held that the admission of evidence of the civil protection from abuse order was relevant and probative on the question of intent and course of conduct. Finally, the court found that defendant's sentence fell within Pennsylvania sentencing guidelines and presented no evidence of bias on the part of the trial judge. The court affirmed the judgment of sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of sentence entered against defendant by the trial court after a jury convicted defendant of stalking. The court found that the evidence of related prior bad acts was admissible.

Demuth v. Miller


No. 00027 Harrisburg 1994


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


438 Pa. Super. 437; 652 A.2d 891; 1995 Pa. Super. LEXIS 20; 67 Empl. Prac. Dec. (CCH) P43,920


June 21, 1994, Argued  
January 11, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Allowance of Appeal and Cross-Petition for Allowance of Appeal Denied September 8, 1995, Reported at: 1995 Pa. LEXIS 711. Certiorari Denied February 20, 1996, Reported at: 1996 U.S. LEXIS 988.
Appeal denied by DeMuth v. Miller, 542 Pa. 634, 665 A.2d 469, 1995 Pa. LEXIS 711 (1995)
Writ of certiorari denied Miller v. DeMuth, 516 U.S. 1114, 133 L. Ed. 2d 846, 116 S. Ct. 916, 1996 U.S. LEXIS 988 (1996)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Judgment of the Court of Common Pleas of Cumberland County, Civil Division at No. 4072 CIVIL 1991.

Appeal from the JUDGMENT ENTERED December 23, 1993, in the Court of Common Pleas of Cumberland County, No. 4072 CIVIL 1991. Before HESS & HOFFER, JJ.
DeMuth v. Miller, 28 Pa. D. & C.4th 161, 1993 Pa. Dist. & Cnty. Dec. LEXIS 9 (1993)



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee sought review of a judgment of the Court of Common Pleas of Cumberland County (Pennsylvania), which rendered judgment in favor of appellee corporation in its action against appellant for soliciting clients after his termination. Appellant brought a crossclaim against appellee for wrongful termination.


OVERVIEW: Appellant employee was hired by appellee employee as a professional management consultant. The business relationship was renewed each year. A provision of the employment contract stated that employer could terminate the contract for cause and in that case there was a penalty provision for any former clients of employer who retained appellant. One of the listed causes for termination was homosexuality. After appellant went on a television representing a gay and lesbian coalition, he was terminated. Appellant opened his own office and solicited former clients. Appellee brought an action against appellant for the loss of business. In a counterclaim, appellant claimed that he had been wrongly terminated. The trial court awarded damages to appellee. On appeal, the court held that the continued relationship between the parties created the inference that the parties assented to another contract for a term of the same length and same conditions. Thus, appellant breached the contract by soliciting clients. The court held that discrimination based on sexual orientation was not actionable under any Pennsylvania statute or its constitution nor did it violate U.S. Const. amend. XIV.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment awarding appellee employer damages in its action against appellant employee for soliciting former clients after his termination. The parties assented to another contract for the same salary upon the same terms and for a similar period of time because they continued the employment relationship after the employment contract expired.

Estate of Pew


No. 1577 Philadelphia 1993, No. 1578 Philadelphia 1993, No. 1579 Philadelphia 1993, No. 1580 Philadelphia 1993, No. 1581 Philadelphia 1993, No. 1812 Philadelphia 1993


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


440 Pa. Super. 195; 655 A.2d 521; 1994 Pa. Super. LEXIS 3787



December 28, 1994, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Allowance of Appeal Withdrawn ( No. 1579 Philadelphia 1993) November 15, 1995. Petition for Allowance of Appeal Discontinued ( No. 1578 Philadelphia 1993, No. 1580 Philadelphia 1993, No. 1812 Philadelphia 1993) April 18, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Decree March 29, 1993, in the Court of Common Pleas of Montgomery County, Orphans, No. 89-908.

Appeal from the Decree March 29, 1993, in the Court of Common Pleas of Montgomery County, Orphans, No. 50940.

Appeal from the Decree March 29, 1993, in the Court of Common Pleas of Montgomery County, Orphans, No. 50940; No. 89-908.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, heirs and devisees, of an estate sought review of a judgment by the Court of Common Pleas of Montgomery County, Orphans' Court (Pennsylvania), which distributed stock to a life beneficiary of a trust. Appellants in consolidated appeals contested the distribution, and challenged the failure of trustees to diversify investments, the failure to disqualify opposing counsel, and the timeliness of a 1986 trust agreement.


OVERVIEW: An inter vivos trust was created for the benefit of two grandsons. Upon each grandson's death, the settlor instructed that the net income from the deceased's portion of the estate was to be paid in equal shares for the support, maintenance and education of his children. In the consolidated appeals before the court, appellants, heirs and devisees of the estate, contended that the trial court erred in distributing ordinary and extraordinary stock dividends to a life beneficiary between 1948 and 1963 pursuant to the Principal and Income Acts of 1945 and 1947, 20 P.S. § 8101 et seq. The court held that the trial court correctly ruled that the dividends should be distributed to the holders of the life estate. The court held that the settlor intended to give her grandsons the stock as well as the cash dividends. The court also affirmed ruling that trustees had properly distributed extraordinary stock dividends to the life beneficiary. The court held that trustees' primary duty was to preserve the estate and that they had acted with reasonable prudence. The court reversed the holding that the 1986 trust agreement was time barred. The decree was affirmed in part, and reversed in part.


OUTCOME: That part of the decree of the trial court that dismissed as untimely admission of the 1986 trust agreement was reversed and the document was directed to be submitted for probate. The decree, as modified was affirmed, because in Pennsylvania, the presumption was that extraordinary stock dividends were from earning and belong to the income beneficiary.

Estate of Coates


No. 03404 Philadelphia 1993, No. 03405 Philadelphia 1993


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


438 Pa. Super. 195; 652 A.2d 331; 1994 Pa. Super. LEXIS 3770


October 20, 1994, Argued  
December 23, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Decree September 20, 1993 in the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, Orphans No. 3679 of 1927. J. Pawelec, Trial Judge.

Appeal from the Decree September 20, 1993 in the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, Orphans No. 332 of 1908. J. Pawelec, Trial Judge.



DISPOSITION: Decrees affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant hospital challenged the final decrees of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), which dismissed appellant's exceptions to the auditing judge's amended adjudications, and affirmed the amended adjudications absolutely. Appellant's action alleged that income interests to the great-grandchildren of appellee estate's testatrix were invalid under the common law rule against perpetuities.


OVERVIEW: The will of appellee estate's testatrix established a trust to pay net income to her daughter for life. Upon her daughter's death, the net income was paid in equal shares to her daughter's children until the death of the last of testatrix's grandchildren at which time the net income would be paid to the testatrix's great-grandchildren per stirpes. Upon the death of the great-grandchildren, one-half of the principal was to be paid to appellant hospital. Appellant brought an action which alleged that the purported income interests to the testatrix's great-grandchildren were invalid under the common law rule against perpetuities. The trial court dismissed appellant's action. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that the remainder interests to the testatrix's great-grandchildren became fixed upon the death of each grandchild, and were therefore valid even though those interests did not vest upon the death of each grandchild. The court ruled that because the remainder interests were valid, they could be separated from possibly void interests under the doctrine of vertical separability, and doing so did not disturb the testatrix's overall testamentary plan.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of appellant hospital's action because the remainder interests to the great-grandchildren of appellee estate's testatrix became fixed upon the death of each grandchild, and were therefore valid. Consequently, the valid remainder interests could be separated from possibly void interests under the doctrine of vertical separability.

Mazaika v. Bank One, N.A.


No. 00231 Philadelphia 1993


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


439 Pa. Super. 95; 653 A.2d 640; 1994 Pa. Super. LEXIS 3612


April 18, 1994, Argued  
December 14, 1994, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Revised January 24, 1995.
Appeal granted by Bank One, N.A. v. Mazaika, 540 Pa. 638, 659 A.2d 557, 1995 Pa. LEXIS 2119 (1995)
Reversed by Bank One v. Mazaika (In re Citibank Credit Card Litig.), 545 Pa. 115, 680 A.2d 845, 1996 Pa. LEXIS 1530 (1996)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Order of the Court of Common Pleas, Civil Division, of Philadelphia County, No. 4058 March Term, 1992. J. Dinubile, Trial Judge.

Appeal from the Order dated December 17, 1992 docketed December 23, 1992 in the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, Civil No. March Term, 1992-4058.
Mazaika v. Bank One, N.A., 1993 Pa. Super. LEXIS 3705 (Pa. Super. Ct., Oct. 29, 1993)
Mazaika v. Bank One, N.A., 637 A.2d 662, 25 Phila. 192, 1992 Phila. Cty. Rptr. LEXIS 129 (Pa. C.P., 1992)



DISPOSITION: Order reversed. Case remanded. Jurisdiction relinquished.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant credit cardholders sought review of a judgment from the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), which dismissed appellants' action brought against appellee national bank. Appellants' action was brought against appellee, which was located in Ohio, because appellee charged appellants annual fees and service fees and characterized these fees as interest pursuant to Ohio law.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to 12 U.S.C.S. § 85 of the National Bank Act, appellant national bank, which was located in Ohio, charged interest at the rate allowed under Ohio law. In accordance with Ohio law, appellee included contingent default charges within its definition of interest. Appellant credit cardholders brought an action challenging the legality of the charges under Pennsylvania's consumer protection laws, and the trial court dismissed appellants' action. Appellants sought review, and the court reversed. Although the charges were lawful under Ohio law and § 85 permitted appellee to charge interest at the rate allowed by Ohio law, the court found that § 85 had not preempted Pennsylvania's consumer protection laws because the term "interest" as employed in § 85 had not been intended to mean anything other than the ordinary and popular meaning of the word "interest." The court found that because the ordinary meaning of the term "interest" had not included contingent default charges, § 85 had not preempted Pennsylvania's consumer protection law dealing with charges and penalties not commonly associated with the term "interest."


OUTCOME: The court reversed a judgment dismissing appellant credit cardholders' action against appellee national bank that was brought after appellee characterized fees as interest pursuant to Ohio law because the National Bank Act, which permitted appellee to charge interest at the rate allowed by Ohio law, had not preempted Pennsylvania's usury and consumer protection laws that dealt with fees and penalties not commonly included in the term interest.

Commonwealth v. Santiago


No. 3757 Philadelphia, 1992


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


439 Pa. Super. 447; 654 A.2d 1062; 1994 Pa. Super. LEXIS 3594


January 19, 1994, Argued  
December 7, 1994, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Allowance of Appeal Denied July 24, 1995, Reported at: 1995 Pa. LEXIS 1913.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Order of the Court of Common Pleas, Criminal Division, of Philadelphia County, Nos. 8509-221-23. Before MAZZOLA, J.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The commonwealth sought review of an order from the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), which barred a retrial of appellant and dismissed murder charges against appellant after the commonwealth failed to make timely disclosure to appellant of certain information alleged to be material and exculpatory.


OVERVIEW: After appellant was convicted for the murder of a police officer, appellant was granted a new trial. During the new trial, appellant received information from the commonwealth which had not been disclosed prior to appellant's initial trial. After appellant filed a motion to dismiss, the trial court barred a retrial of appellant and dismissed the charges of murder against appellant because the commonwealth had failed to make a timely disclosure of certain information alleged to be material and exculpatory. The commonwealth sought review, and the court reversed. The court found that the information which had not been disclosed by the commonwealth had been neither exculpatory nor material to appellant's defense. Therefore, the court held that the commonwealth's failure to disclose these items had not violated the Brady rule. Furthermore, the court found that even if the information had been material, the withholding of evidence had not approached the egregious nature of prosecutorial misconduct that was required to prohibit retrial under the Double Jeopardy Clause of the Pennsylvania Constitution.


OUTCOME: The court reversed an order barring a retrial of appellant and dismissing murder charges against appellant because the commonwealth's disclosure of information after appellant's initial trial and during appellant's re-trial for murder had not violated appellant's due process rights under the Brady rule. The commonwealth's delayed disclosure had not violated the Brady rule because the information had been neither exculpatory nor material.

Commonwealth v. Berryman


No. 584 Philadelphia 1993


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


437 Pa. Super. 258; 649 A.2d 961; 1994 Pa. Super. LEXIS 3288


April 18, 1994, Argued  
November 1, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Allowance of Appeal Denied June 27, 1995, Reported at: 1995 Pa. LEXIS 2420.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Order January 15, 1993, in the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, Criminal, No. 9209-2260. Before QUINONES, J.



DISPOSITION: Vacated and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant commonwealth sought review of the decision from the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania) in which the trial court sentenced appellee to probation after he pled nolo contendere to charges of selling crack cocaine in violation of 35 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 780-113. The trial court did not first render a verdict on the crime pursuant to 35 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 780-117(1)(vi).


OVERVIEW: Appellee was charged with selling two vials of crack cocaine to an undercover police officer in violation of 35 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 780-113. After his plea of nolo contendere, the court granted him a sentence of probation without a verdict, pursuant to 35 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 780-117(1)(vi). Appellant commonwealth sought review of the sentencing determination by the trial court, claiming that the court had incorrectly interpreted the sentencing statute and the result was to allow those charged with drug dealing to more lenient treatment. Appellee claimed that the prosecutor had committed misconduct by practicing selective enforcement and that he had been denied equal protection and substantive due process. The court agreed with appellant the trial court had incorrectly interpreted the sentencing statute and that appellee should not have received the sentencing of probation without verdict. The sentence was vacated and remanded for resentencing, though the court did further state that, once correctly interpreted, the statute did pass constitutional muster and the prosecutor had not committed misconduct.


OUTCOME: The court vacated appellee's sentence of probation without verdict and remanded for resentencing. In interpreting the statute allowing probation, the court found that the verdict against appellee was required and that there was no prosecutorial misconduct in bringing the charges against appellee because the prosecutor enjoyed wide discretion pertaining to charges, but not to sentences.

COMMONWEALTH v. STIVALA


No. 01791 Pittsburgh 1992


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


435 Pa. Super. 176; 645 A.2d 257; 1994 Pa. Super. LEXIS 2294


March 17, 1994, Argued  
July 26, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Allowance of Appeal and/or Cross-Petition Denied December 9, 1994.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the decision of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County (Pennsylvania), convicting appellant of arson and sentencing him to imprisonment for four to twelve years.

He was sentenced to imprisonment for four to twelve years. The appellate court affirmed the order because appellant received a fair trial and his due process rights were protected.

Also, jury instruction accurately reflected the law and did not improperly implicate appellant's silence.

Miller v. Hellman


NO. 438 HARRISBURG 1993, NO. 484 HARRISBURG 1993


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


433 Pa. Super. 539; 641 A.2d 592; 1994 Pa. Super. LEXIS 1038



April 8, 1994, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Allowance of Appeal Denied February 22, 1995, Reported at: 1995 Pa. LEXIS 142.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order entered May 17, 1993 docketed May 25, 1993 in the Court of Common Pleas of Perry County, Civil Division, at No. 88-408.

Appeal from the Judgment entered June 28, 1993 in the Court of Common Pleas of Perry County, Civil Division, at No. 88-408.
Miller v. Hellman, 21 Pa. D. & C.4th 462, 1993 Pa. Dist. & Cnty. Dec. LEXIS 93 (1993)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, victim and wife, challenged an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Perry County, Civil Division (Pennsylvania), which denied its petition for delay damages under Pa. R. Civ. P. 238, after a jury awarded damages greater than the insurance policy limits of appellee, estate of the deceased at-fault driver, in appellant's action for injuries sustained after an automobile accident.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, victim and wife, brought an action against appellee, estate for the deceased at-fault driver, for injuries sustained after an automobile accident. After a jury trial, judgment was entered in favor of appellants, in excess of appellee's insurance policy limits. Appellants then brought a petition against appellees for delay damages. The trial court denied the petition, finding that the tender of policy limits by appellee's insurer within the time period set forth in Pa. R. Civ. P. 238 precluded such damages. The appellate court reversed and remanded, holding that appellee would be liable for delay damages if it did not tender all its assets to settle the claim. On remand, the trial court was directed to hold an evidentiary hearing to determine if appellee's estate could have offered more assets. However, the appellate court declined to hold appellee's insurer liable for such damages, holding that the tender of limits was sufficient, and that the insurer was not obligated to deposit the monies with the trial court. Further, the appellate court held that appellee's challenge to the constitutionality of Pa. R. Civ. P. 238 was spurious.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed and remanded the trial court's order that denied award of delay damages to appellants, victim and wife, after a jury awarded damages greater than the insurance policy limits of appellee, estate of the deceased at-fault driver, in appellant's action for injuries sustained after an automobile accident, because, to avoid such damages, appellee was required to tender all of its assets to settle the claim.

Commonwealth v. McClintock


No. 01833 PITTSBURGH, 1992


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


433 Pa. Super. 83; 639 A.2d 1222; 1994 Pa. Super. LEXIS 1176



April 7, 1994, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence in the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County, Criminal Division, No. 9104971, 9109745, 9104711. OTN: C6111070, C7149516



DISPOSITION: Judgment of sentence affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County, Criminal Division (Pennsylvania), which convicted him of luring a child into a motor vehicle, 18 Pa. Const. Stat. § 2910, interfering with child custody, 18 Pa. Const. Stat. § 2904, and two counts of criminal attempt to lure a child into his vehicle, 18 Pa. Const. Stat. § 901.


OVERVIEW: After a bench trial, appellant was convicted of luring a child into a motor vehicle, 18 Pa. Const. Stat. § 2910, interfering with child custody, 18 Pa. Const. Stat. § 2904, and two counts of criminal attempt to lure a child into his vehicle, 18 Pa. Const. Stat. § 901. The appellate court affirmed, holding that the evidence was sufficient to support the conviction under § 901. In so ruling, the appellate court held that appellant's hand motions, or waves, constituted a substantial step necessary toward the commission of the offense. The appellate court also held that the evidence was sufficient to support the conviction under § 2904. In so ruling, the appellate court held that the trial court's extension of the scope of § 2904, to protect children from the unlawful taking of individuals who were not their parents, custodians, or guardians, was permissible. Further, the appellate court held that photographs of appellant's vehicle were properly authenticated. Also, an officer's testimony regarding the license plate number recited to him by a victim was properly admitted. Lastly, the appellate court held that the term "lure" in § 2910 was specific and definite.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's conviction of appellant for luring a child into a motor vehicle, interfering with child custody, and two counts of criminal attempt to lure a child into his vehicle, because appellant's wave to the children was a substantial step toward the commission of the offense, the extension of interference with child custody to non-parents was permissible, and the term lure was specific and definite.

Witcher v. Witcher


No. 02543 PHL 1993


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


433 Pa. Super. 14; 639 A.2d 1187; 1994 Pa. Super. LEXIS 883


January 20, 1994, Argued  
April 4, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Allowance of Appeal Denied August 12, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the order entered June 25, 1993. In the Court of Common Pleas of Delaware County, Civil, No. 87-9363. Before LABRUM, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant ex-wife challenged an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Delaware County, Civil (Pennsylvania), which granted appellee ex-husband's petition for a no-fault divorce, pursuant to Pa. Const. Stat. Ann. §§ 3301(c), (d), awarded equitable distribution of the estate, and denied appellant's counter-claim for alimony, attorney's fees, costs, expenses, and for a fault divorce, pursuant to 23 Pa. Const. Stat. Ann. § 3301(a)(1), (2), (3).


OVERVIEW: Appellee ex-husband brought a no-fault divorce action against appellant ex-wife, pursuant to Pa. Const. Stat. Ann. §§ 3301(c), (d). Appellant counter-claimed for alimony, attorney's fees, costs, expenses, and for a fault divorce, pursuant to 23 Pa. Const. Stat. Ann. § 3301(a)(1), (2), (3). The trial court granted a no-fault divorce, awarded equitable distribution of the estate, and denied appellant's other requests. In affirming, the appellate court stated that appellant waived her claims regarding equitable distribution as she failed to file a motion for post-trial relief as required by Pa. R. Civ. P. 227.1. Nonetheless, appellant's constitutional arguments with respect to the award and proceedings were meritless. It was not a violation of U.S. Const. amend. V and XIV to allow evidence of marital misconduct to be heard in regard to an award of alimony, 23 Pa. Const. Stat. Ann. § 3701, but not in regard to equitable distribution, 23 Pa. Const. Stat. Ann. § 3502. Further, appellant was not deprived of any benefits to which she was statutorily entitled, as the trial court carefully considered appellant's needs and sources of income when it made its award.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's order that granted appellee ex-husband's petition for a no-fault divorce, awarded equitable distribution of the estate, and denied appellant ex-wife's counter-claim for alimony, attorney's fees, costs, expenses, and for a fault divorce, because appellant failed to preserve her claims of error and appellee's constitutional arguments with respect to the award and proceedings were meritless.

Commonwealth v. Lee


No. 00581 Harrisburg 1993


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


432 Pa. Super. 414; 638 A.2d 1006; 1994 Pa. Super. LEXIS 780


February 7, 1994, Submitted  
March 16, 1994, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Allowance of Appeal Denied August 16, 1994, Reported at: 1994 Pa. LEXIS 381.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the JUDGMENT OF SENTENCE July 6, 1993, Docketed July 7, 1993, in the Court of Common Pleas of Centre County, CRIMINAL No. 1991 - 1032. Before GRINE, J.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant criminal sought review from a judgment of the Court of Common Pleas of Centre County (Pennsylvania), which convicted appellant of rape and involuntary deviate sexual intercourse in a case brought by appellee, the commonwealth of Pennsylvania.


OVERVIEW: Appellant criminal challenged his convictions for rape and involuntary deviate sexual intercourse (IDSI). Appellant argued that the evidence of rape was insufficient because the victim submitted to the sexual acts, thus allowing no inference that there was forcible compulsion. The court found that the victim feared for his life if he did not submit, which was sufficient to prove forcible compulsion beyond a reasonable doubt. Appellant complained that a floor brush was improperly admitted. The court held that there was a sufficient foundation for the brush's admission. Appellant also argued that letters were improperly admitted into evidence because they were not authenticated. The court held that a witness acknowledged that he was familiar with appellant's handwriting and identified the letter, and that this was sufficient to authenticate it. The court held, however, that the trial court imposed an illegal sentence by punishing appellant twice for each act of penile penetration, in violation of the double jeopardy clause of the United States Constitution. The court vacated the sentences for IDSI imposed concurrent to the sentences for rape, and otherwise affirmed the judgment.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the sentences for involuntary deviate sexual intercourse (IDSI) and otherwise affirmed the judgment of appellant criminal convicted of rape and IDSI in a case brought by the commonwealth of Pennsylvania. The court held that there was sufficient evidence to prove forcible compulsion and a witness properly authenticated a letter, but appellant was punished twice for each act in violation of the double jeopardy clause.

Commonwealth v. Adamo

SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


431 Pa. Super. 529; 637 A.2d 302; 1994 Pa. Super. LEXIS 270

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence entered April 16, 1993, Court of Common Pleas, Bucks County, Criminal Division at No. 1185/1992. Before SCOTT, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his conviction by the Court of Common Pleas, Bucks County (Pennsylvania), for criminal attempt to lure a child into a motor vehicle in violation of 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. §§ 901, 2910.


OVERVIEW: The intended victim testified that he was approached by appellant and offered one thousand dollars for one-half hour of work. The intended victim also testified that appellant would not tell him the kind of work involved unless he accompanied appellant to his car. The court affirmed appellant's conviction of attempt to lure a child into a motor vehicle because the intent of appellant to lure his planned victim into his car was apparent. The court agreed with the determination of the trial court that there was evidence to prove each of the elements of attempt beyond a reasonable doubt. The court also held that the Child Luring Statute, 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 2910, was constitutional and that it was not vague as applied to appellant since appellant himself had articulated to his intended victim that his behavior was criminally proscribed. Balancing the factors in the present case, the court further concluded that appellant's trial delay was not inordinate and that appellant bore the responsibility for the bulk of that delay. In the absence of a showing of prejudice, the dismissal of charges for failure to comply with Pa. R. Crim. P. 1122 was not required.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction of appellant for criminal attempt to lure a child into a motor vehicle because it found that the evidence proved each element of the crime, the statutory proscription was constitutional, and appellant was not denied his speedy trial rights.

Commonwealth v. Gautieri


No. 00602 Philadelphia 1993


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


431 Pa. Super. 412; 636 A.2d 1153; 1994 Pa. Super. LEXIS 189


December 15, 1993, Argued  
February 1, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Judgment of Sentence February 17, 1993, in the Court of Common Pleas of Bucks County, Criminal, No. 4927-01 of 1992.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment by the Court of Common Pleas of Bucks County (Pennsylvania), that convicted him of statutory rape, indecent assault, corruption of minors, and involuntary deviate sexual intercourse.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of statutory rape, indecent assault, corruption of minors, and involuntary deviate sexual intercourse (IDSI) perpetrated against his 12-year-old nephew. Appellant only challenged his conviction for IDSI, 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 3123(5). Most of his complaints were constitutional in nature. In affirming the judgment, the court held that the statutory rape statute, 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 3122, was a more general statute than the IDSI statute. Second, the more general statute, statutory rape, contained an element outside of the more specific. The court held that since the general statute was not encompassed by the more specific, there was no bar against the state pursuing convictions for both offenses. Appellant next contended that the IDSI statute violated U.S. Const. amend IV, the equal protection clause, because it irrationally discriminated against unmarried, consenting couples, where one of the individuals is under the age of sixteen, homosexuals, who are unable to marry, and adolescents. Appellant had no standing to assert these claims. Even if appellant did have standing, the court found that the IDSI statute was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that convicted appellant of statutory rape, indecent assault, corruption of minors, and involuntary deviate sexual intercourse (IDSI) because it found that there was no bar to the prosecution under the IDSI statute and the complained of statute was constitutional.

Commonwealth v. Plass


No. 1014 Pittsburgh 1992


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


431 Pa. Super. 251; 636 A.2d 637; 1994 Pa. Super. LEXIS 1


September 8, 1993, Argued  
January 4, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Allowance of Appeal and/or Cross-Petition Granted May 18, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the ORDER Entered May 28, 1992, in the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County, Criminal No. CC 9111528.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant commonwealth challenged the sentence given by the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County (Pennsylvania), which convicted appellee offender of possession, and possession with intent to deliver, cocaine. The trial court refused to apply the mandatory minimum sentence, reasoning that since the first conviction did not occur before the second offense, an enhancement was improper.


OVERVIEW: After reconsidering appellee offender's sentence for possession, and possession with intent to deliver, cocaine, in a case of first impression, the court held that at the time of sentencing appellee had been convicted of another drug trafficking offense, and the trial court was required to impose the enhanced sentence. The court found the language of 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 7508(a)(3)(i) to be unambiguous. The court explained that the legislature did not adopt the traditional look-back rule when drafting this recidivist provision, but rather made it clear that the relevant look-back period began at the time of sentencing. The court rejected the claim that the statute violated equal protection, holding that it was reasonably designed to effectuate the purpose it sought to achieve. The court also rejected the claim that potential disparate treatment caused by administrative delay rendered the statute unconstitutional, and it recommended seeking appropriate remedies if, in an isolated case, an unfairly harsh sentence were to occur. The sentence was vacated and the cause remanded for resentencing.


OUTCOME: The sentence was vacated, and the case was remanded to the trial court for imposition of a new sentence in accordance with the court's opinion. The statute was unambiguous, the relevant look-back period began at the time of sentencing, and appellee offender should have received the sentence enhancement.

Commonwealth v. Rogers


No. 1557 Pittsburgh, 1992


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


430 Pa. Super. 253; 634 A.2d 245; 1993 Pa. Super. LEXIS 3744


April 14, 1993, Argued  
November 17, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Judgment of Sentence of the Court of Common Pleas, Criminal Division, of Venango County, No. 534 of 1991.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant restaurant owner sought review of the judgment from the Court of Common Pleas of Venango County (Pennsylvania), which found appellant guilty of erecting a sign without the approval of the Pennsylvania Department of Transportation and which penetrated the approach to an airport runway in violation of 74 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 5701(a)-(b) in a trial de novo upon appeal from appellant's conviction in a lower court.


OVERVIEW: Appellant restaurant owner was cited for violating 74 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 5701(a)-(b) when he erected a 95 foot sign without first obtaining the approval of the Pennsylvania Department of Transportation (PennDot) and which penetrated the approach area to an airport runway. After his conviction at a lower court, appellant was tried de novo before the trial court and again was found guilty. On appeal, appellant argued that the enforcement of § 5701 was an unconstitutional taking of his property without just compensation in violation of U.S. Const. amend. V. in the absence of an air easement or a zoning ordinance regulating the height of signs. The court affirmed the conviction. The court held that enforcement of § 5701 was not an unconstitutional taking of property because appellant was convicted for not obtaining PennDot's prior approval to erect the sign. The court held that only when PennDot refused to allow the sign would a claim for a taking arise. The court also found that § 5701was a proper exercise of the state's police power to identify potential hazards and to prevent obstructions to air traffic, thereby ensuring the safe operation of airports.


OUTCOME: Judgment convicting appellant restaurant owner for erecting a sign which penetrated the approach to an airport runway was affirmed, because enforcement of the statute was not an unconstitutional taking where the violation was the failure to obtain approval for the sign from Pennsylvania's transportation agency and because the statute was a proper exercise of the state's police power to ensure the safety of airport operations.

Commonwealth v. Torres


NO. 01058 PHL 92, NO. 01071 PHL 92


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


429 Pa. Super. 228; 632 A.2d 319; 1993 Pa. Super. LEXIS 3624


May 12, 1993, Argued  
October 28, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Allowance of Appeal Denied April 29, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Order entered February 17, 1992 in the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, Criminal Division, at No. 9111-1294-1301. Before LYNN, J.

Appeal from the Order entered February 17, 1992 in the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, at No. 9111-1310-17. Before LYNN, J.
Commonwealth v. Torres, 16 Pa. D. & C.4th 564, 1993 Pa. Dist. & Cnty. Dec. LEXIS 268 (1993)



DISPOSITION: Order to suppress the evidence reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The commonwealth sought review of an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, Criminal Division, Pennsylvania, which granted defendants' motion to suppress evidence resulting from a warrantless search.


OVERVIEW: Defendants, who were charged after police found stolen vehicles in their possession in an autobody shop, filed a motion to suppress based on lack of probable cause to search. The trial court granted the motion. On appeal, the court reversed, and held that police officers did not need a warrant to walk onto commercial property that was open to the public. The court explained that the U.S. Const. amend. IV protection against unreasonable searches extended to commercial property; however, an individual was required to first show that he had a legitimate expectation of privacy in the area being searched. Mere looking at that which was open to view was not a search. Defendants did not have a legitimate expectation of privacy in the garage driveway, nor were their privacy rights offended by the officer's peering through the garage's open door. The shop was open to the public, and the police arrived during regular business hours. Secondly, the court ruled that the record contained no testimony to support the inference that one of the officers entered the garage before consent to search was given. Consent was given by one in authority, and that obviated the need for a search warrant.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the grant of defendants' motion to suppress because police officers entering commercial property open to the public during regular business hours did not need a search warrant, and in any case, consent to search was given by one in authority.

Morgan Guar. Trust Co. v. Staats

SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA

February 9, 1993, Argued  
September 16, 1993, Filed

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Order Entered May 7, 1992, in the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County, Civil, No. G.D. No. 92-6219. Before FRIEDMAN, J.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, who had executed a promissory note, sought review of a judgment of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County (Pennsylvania), which denied appellants their petition for a rule upon appellee, the assignee of the promissory note, to show cause why the execution proceeding should not be stayed or to set aside the execution of the judgment against appellants. The judgment had been transferred from a sister state.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, who had executed a promissory note, defaulted on the note after it had been transferred by the original holder to appellee, the assignee of the promissory note. Appellants also executed an estoppel letter and assumption agreement, which contained express waivers and made them personally liable on the note. Appellee filed suit in another state to enforce payment on the note, and was granted unopposed summary judgment. The judgment was transferred to Pennsylvania and writs of execution were issued directing the sale of appellants' properties. Appellants petitioned the trial court for a rule upon appellee to show cause why the execution proceeding should not be stayed or to set aside the execution, which was denied. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 3305. Finally, the default judgment was res judicata with regard to transactions occurring prior to entry of judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment against appellants, who had executed a promissory note, and held that they failed to merit a stay of execution or a set-aside of the execution on the transferred judgment. Appellee, assignee of the executory note, was a holder in due course, and took the note free of all defenses appellants had. The court also concluded that doctrine of res judicata precludes a collateral attack by appellants.

DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded for a new trial on all charges except those for conspiracy to commit third degree murder and the two counts of conspiracy to commit aggravated assault. With respect to such conspiracy charges, judgment is arrested and the charges are dismissed. Jurisdiction is not retained.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment of the Court of Common Pleas, Criminal Division, Berks County (Pennsylvania), which sentenced him to life imprisonment and additional consecutive sentences for first degree murder, conspiracy to commit third degree murder, conspiracy to commit aggravated assault, and carrying a firearm without a license.


OVERVIEW: Appellant argued that insufficient evidence sustained his convictions for first degree murder, conspiracy to commit third degree murder, conspiracy to commit aggravated assault, and carrying a firearm without a license. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded for a new trial on all charges except for conspiracy to commit third degree murder and the two counts of conspiracy to commit aggravated assault. With respect to such conspiracy charges, judgment was arrested and the charges were dismissed. The trial court's error in fashioning a jury instruction according to the language of 18 Pa. Const. Stat. § 6104 without qualification relieved the commonwealth of its burden of proof and was reversible error. The alleged prosecutorial misconduct did not warrant a mistrial. Appellant's co-conspirator's testimony on his plea agreement was not an attempt to comment on appellant's failure to testify at trial.


OUTCOME: Regarding appellant's convictions for first degree murder, conspiracy to commit third degree murder, conspiracy to commit aggravated assault, and carrying a firearm without a license, the court reversed and remanded for new trial on all charges except those for conspiracy to commit third degree murder and aggravated assault. Regarding those conspiracy charges, judgment was arrested and the charges were dismissed for insufficient evidence.

Commonwealth v. Barnes


NO. 210 PITTSBURGH 1992, NO. 211 PITTSBURGH 1992


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


427 Pa. Super. 326; 629 A.2d 123; 1993 Pa. Super. LEXIS 2367


January 7, 1993, Argued  
July 22, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence Entered January 27, 1992, in the Court of Common Pleas, Criminal Division, of Erie County, No. 1797 of 1991.

Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence Entered January 27, 1992, in the Court of Common Pleas, Criminal Division, of Erie County, No. 1798 of 1991. Before BOZZA, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgments of sentence affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants sought review of their convictions, which were entered by the Court of Common Pleas, Criminal Division, of Erie County (Pennsylvania), on seven counts of cruelty to animals, in violation of 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 5511(c).


OVERVIEW: Subsequent to their conviction for cruelty to animals in violation of 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 5511(c), appellants claimed that the grant of police power to the Erie Humane Society, a private corporation that initiated the prosecution, was an improper delegation of governmental authority. Appellants also claimed that § 5511(c) was unconstitutionally vague, and that the evidence was insufficient to support their convictions. In affirming the convictions, the court held that appellant's improper delegation claim was without merit. The court found that the society's police power to initiate criminal proceedings was circumscribed by the rules of criminal procedure. The court held that the statute was not unconstitutionally vague because persons of common intelligence could conclude that appellants' utter neglect of their horses would not be considered as activity undertaken in normal agricultural operations. Finally, the court concluded that appellants' sufficiency of the evidence claim was without merit because they failed in their burden to establish that their activities were normal agricultural operations.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellants' conviction for cruelty to animals. The court held that appellant's improper delegation claim was without merit because, although a private corporation, the Erie Humane Society, which initiated the prosecution, was statutorily vested with police power through the rules of criminal procedure. The court also held that that the statute under which appellants were convicted was not unconstitutionally vague.

Commonwealth v. Urbanski


NO. 03191 PHILADELPHIA 1991


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


426 Pa. Super. 505; 627 A.2d 789; 1993 Pa. Super. LEXIS 2251


February 19, 1993, Argued  
July 8, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Allowance of Appeal Denied October 19, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence September 20, 1991, In the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, Criminal, No. 9010-2358, 2360, 2361, 2365, 2366.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of sentence affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania) that convicted appellant of third-degree murder, homicide by vehicle while driving under the influence, driving under the influence of alcohol or a controlled substance, aggravated assault, and recklessly endangering another person. Appellant alleged that the blood alcohol test that was administered was improper.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was the driver of a car that veered off the road, killing appellant's wife. Appellant was found guilty of third-degree murder, homicide by vehicle while driving under the influence, driving under the influence of alcohol or a controlled substance, aggravated assault and recklessly endangering another person. The court affirmed, holding that the blood alcohol test administered at the hospital was proper pursuant to 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 1547(a)(1). The court held that where a police officer had reasonable grounds to believe that a person was driving under the influence of alcohol, he could require an individual to submit to a chemical test without a warrant. The court held that there was sufficient evidence to prove that appellant's actions were the direct cause of his wife's death, as causation was proved. The evidence also was sufficient to establish malice. Appellant's ineffective assistance of counsel claims failed because the evidence of appellant's intoxicated condition was overwhelming and the admission of his suspended license did not influence the verdict.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a judgment of the trial court that convicted appellant of third-degree murder, homicide by vehicle while driving under the influence, driving under the influence of alcohol, aggravated assault, and recklessly endangering another person, holding that the blood alcohol test that was administered was proper. There was sufficient evidence to show that appellant acted with malice and caused his wife's death.

Dansby v. Thomas Jefferson Univ. Hosp.


No. 706 Philadelphia, 1992


SUPERIOR COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


424 Pa. Super. 549; 623 A.2d 816; 1993 Pa. Super. LEXIS 950


September 23, 1992, Argued  
March 19, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected. Petition for Allowance of Appeal Denied November 3, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Order of the Court of Common Pleas, Civil Division, of Montgomery County, No. 90-21237. Before OTT, J.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff mother and father challenged a decision by the Court of Common Pleas, Civil Division, of Montgomery County (Pennsylvania), which held that their wrongful birth action against defendant doctors was barred by Pennsylvania's wrongful birth statute, 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 8305(a). Plaintiffs further sought review of the trial court's decision to sustain defendants' demurrer to plaintiffs' complaint.


OVERVIEW: When plaintiff mother became pregnant, defendant doctors recommended amniocentesis testing to determine whether there were any fetal defects. After the test was performed, defendants advised plaintiff mother and father that plaintiff mother was carrying a normal fetus. After plaintiffs' daughter was born with severe birth defects, it was discovered that the amniotic fluid that was tested by defendants did not belong to plaintiff mother. Plaintiffs filed a wrongful birth lawsuit against defendants for failing to perform an amniocentesis test. The defendants filed preliminary objections in the nature of a demurrer in which they asserted that an action for wrongful birth was precluded by 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 8305(a). The trial court sustained defendants' demurrer. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's decision, holding that § 8305(a) was not unconstitutional, because it did not impose a restriction upon a woman's right to an abortion. The court further found that § 8305(a) did not violate the Equal Protection Clause of the U.S. Const. Amend. XIV, because entitlement to monetary damages because of another's negligence has never been held to be a fundamental right.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision to sustain defendant doctors' demurrer, holding that plaintiff mother and father's wrongful birth action was barred by 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 8305(a). The court further found that § 8305(a), which barred causes of action for wrongful births, was constitutional, and did not violate the Equal Protection Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment.
